## [2026-05-18 19:30 CDT] - US-016
- Implemented per-app planner networking and provider-exec healthcheck contract. `AppPlanner.plan` now emits a single per-app `NetworkPlan` (`lando-<slug>`, `shared: false`, `driver: "bridge"`) on every app with at least one service; zero-service apps still emit `networks: []`. Planner now applies user-authored `service.healthcheck` on top of the service-type default via a new `applyAuthoredHealthcheck` seam (mirroring `applyAuthoredAppMount`) so `service.healthcheck` reaches `ServicePlan.healthcheck` even for service types that emit nothing (node, postgres, redis, etc.). The planner then gates non-provider-exec healthcheck kinds: any service with `healthcheck.kind` set to anything other than `"command"` or `"none"` fails with `CapabilityError({ service, feature: "healthcheck kind <k>", capability: "serviceHealth", providerId, remediation })`. Catalog service-type defaults (`apache`, `nginx`, `php`, `python`, `ruby`, `static`) switched from `kind: "tcp"` to `kind: "command"` with a portable `bash -c "exec 3<>/dev/tcp/127.0.0.1/<port>"` TCP probe so the same exec-based runner can drive them. `renderStartAppResult` is now inspect-state-derived: it renders `ready: <app>` only when every `result.servicesStarted` entry's `state` is in `{running, ready}`, otherwise `starting: <app>` (the per-service `<name> (<state>) <endpoints>` body is unchanged).
- Files changed: `core/src/services/planner.ts` (per-app `NetworkPlan` emission, `appNetworkName` slug helper, `applyAuthoredHealthcheck` override seam, planner-time `serviceHealth` capability gate); `core/src/cli/commands/start.ts` (inspect-state-derived readiness banner); `plugins/service-lando/src/services/{apache,nginx,php,python,ruby,static}.ts` (`kind: "command"` healthcheck emissions with `bash`/`/dev/tcp` probe); `core/test/services/app-planner.test.ts` (new tests for multi-service per-app network, single-service per-app network with slug sanitization, zero-service `networks: []`, `kind: "tcp"` rejection, `kind: "http"` rejection, authored `kind: "command"` override); `core/test/cli/start.scenario.test.ts` (new tests for `starting:` prefix when a service is not in a ready state, `ready:` prefix when services are in `ready` state); `plugins/service-lando/test/{apache,nginx,php,python,ruby,registration}.test.ts` (healthcheck assertions updated from `kind: "tcp" + port` to `kind: "command" + command: ["bash", "-c", "exec 3<>/dev/tcp/127.0.0.1/<port>"]`); `AGENTS.md` (documented healthcheck/network/readiness contract); `spec/alpha/prd.json`; `spec/alpha/progress.txt`.
- Verification run and result: lsp diagnostics clean for changed TypeScript files; `bun run typecheck` passed; `bun run lint` passed (293 files, no fixes); focused `bun test core/test/services/app-planner.test.ts core/test/cli/start.scenario.test.ts plugins/service-lando/test/{apache,nginx,php,python,ruby,static,registration}.test.ts` passed (79 pass, 1 skip, 0 fail, 361 expect calls); full `bun test --concurrency=1` passed (461 pass, 11 skip, 0 fail, 2417 expect calls). Inline planner manual QA against a 2-service Landofile (`nginx`, `python:3.12`) confirmed `appPlan.networks` = `[{ name: "lando-us016-demo", shared: false, driver: "bridge" }]` and both services emit `kind: "command"` healthchecks with the expected `bash`/`/dev/tcp` probe; a separate run of a user-authored `kind: "tcp"` healthcheck failed closed with `CapabilityError` (service=web, feature="healthcheck kind tcp", capability=serviceHealth, providerId=lando, remediation citing `kind: command`). Per the planner-rejection-runs-after-provider-config gotcha in AGENTS.md, end-to-end CLI verification on a host without a configured runtime provider fails earlier with `ProviderConfigError`, so the canonical verification surface is the planner unit tests, which all pass.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: user-authored `service.healthcheck` overrides should apply at the planner layer (`applyAuthoredHealthcheck`) rather than inside every catalog service type. Service types stay simple (emit a sensible default or nothing), and the planner becomes the single seam where the §6.7 `kind` capability gate fires. This mirrors the existing `applyAuthoredAppMount` pattern.
  - Patterns discovered: emitting a per-app `NetworkPlan` from the planner is the contract surface for §6.6 networking even though current provider apply layers still derive their network name from `plan.slug`. Future work (doctor renderings, multi-network apps) reads the planned list; provider derivation stays as a defensive fallback.
  - Gotchas encountered: existing service-type tests asserted the legacy `kind: "tcp" + port` shape across six files plus `registration.test.ts`; converting them to `kind: "command" + command: ["bash", "-c", "exec 3<>/dev/tcp/127.0.0.1/<port>"]` had to happen in the same commit as the planner gate, or the service-type defaults would self-trigger the new `CapabilityError`. A perl/regex sweep across the test/source pairs is reliable here because every emission and every assertion uses the same template literal pattern keyed on the resolved endpoint port.
  - Gotchas encountered: the `renderStartAppResult` prefix flipping from hardcoded `ready:` to inspect-derived `ready:`/`starting:` does NOT break the existing 2-service start scenario test because the mock provider returns `state: "running"` for every service and the new gate treats `running` as ready. Tests that want to exercise the negative path must explicitly construct a `StartAppResult` with at least one non-`running`/`ready` service state — there is no public seam to make the live provider mock return a stopped state without breaking the apply-then-inspect flow.
  - Useful context: `bash`/`/dev/tcp` remains the lowest-friction portable TCP probe for Debian-derived catalog defaults (`php:apache`, `python:slim`, `ruby:slim`), while Alpine-based defaults (`httpd:2.4-alpine`, `nginx:1.26-alpine`, `caddy:2-alpine`) now use `sh -c "nc -z 127.0.0.1 <port>"` so the default healthcheck works without a bash dependency. The `nc -z` form only checks that the TCP port accepts connections, keeping the probe protocol-agnostic.

- Files reviewed: `core/src/services/planner.ts` (per-app `NetworkPlan`, `appNetworkName`, `applyAuthoredHealthcheck`, `serviceHealth` capability gate), `core/src/cli/commands/start.ts` (inspect-state-derived readiness banner via `isStartAppReady` + `READY_STATES`), `core/test/services/app-planner.test.ts` (new network + healthcheck-rejection tests), `core/test/cli/start.scenario.test.ts` (new starting/ready prefix tests), `plugins/service-lando/src/services/{apache,nginx,php,python,ruby,static}.ts` and matching tests + `registration.test.ts` (catalog defaults flipped to `kind: "command"`), `AGENTS.md` (3 new contract entries), `spec/alpha/prd.json`.
- Findings (no fixes applied — no in-scope defects identified):
  - Cross-checked `appNetworkName(appName)` against the provider's `networkName(plan) = lando-${plan.slug}.replace(/[^a-zA-Z0-9_.-]/gu, "-")` in `plugins/provider-lando/src/{bring-up,bring-down,exec,inspect,logs}.ts`; both sanitize with the same regex and `slug: appName` is set on `decodeAppPlan(...)`, so the planner-emitted network name matches what providers derive from `plan.slug` for every input.
  - Capability gate fires on `servicePlanWithCapabilityRealization.healthcheck` after `applyAuthoredHealthcheck` runs, so user-authored `kind: "tcp"`/`kind: "http"` overrides are caught even on service types (node, postgres, redis) that emit no default healthcheck.
  - `kind: "none"` is permitted by the gate alongside `kind: "command"` — matches the §6.7 schema literal and is the intentional opt-out path for users who want to disable healthchecks.
  - `isStartAppReady` requires `servicesStarted.length > 0`, so a degenerate zero-service app renders `starting:` rather than `ready:`; the planner only emits a network when `services.length > 0`, so the empty-app path is consistent end-to-end.
  - Catalog defaults still emit the `bash`/`/dev/tcp` probe via `endpointPort`, but every catalog source now sets `kind: "command"` and the corresponding tests assert the exact 3-element command array — no remaining `kind: "tcp"` emissions or assertions across `service-lando`.
  - No rejections to record: `review-work` raised no actionable findings during my pass and no orthogonal repo conventions are violated by the diff.
- Acceptance check vs PRD-02 US-016: AC#1 (per-app network for multi-service apps) — `core/test/services/app-planner.test.ts` adds three planner tests (`emits a per-app bridge network for multi-service apps`, single-service slug sanitization, zero-service `networks: []`) — pass. AC#2 (healthcheck limited to provider-exec with clear rejection) — two new planner tests assert `kind: "tcp"` and `kind: "http"` rejection with `CapabilityError(service, feature, capability=serviceHealth, providerId, remediation containing "kind: command")` — pass. AC#3 (`lando start` readiness uses inspect state) — `start.scenario.test.ts` adds positive (`ready:` when all services in `{running, ready}`) and negative (`starting:` when any service `stopped`) tests against `renderStartAppResult` — pass. AC#4-6 (tests/typecheck/lint) — pass.
- Verification run and result: re-ran `bun run typecheck` (passed), `bun run lint` (293 files, no fixes), and focused `bun test core/test/services/app-planner.test.ts core/test/cli/start.scenario.test.ts plugins/service-lando/test/{apache,nginx,php,python,ruby,static,registration}.test.ts` (79 pass, 1 skip, 0 fail, 361 expect calls). Build step's full `bun test --concurrency=1` run (461 pass, 11 skip, 0 fail) covers the broader regression surface; no changes since then.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: when a planner emits a contract surface that providers also derive locally (network names, container names), keep the sanitization regex byte-for-byte identical at both sides. The §6.6 contract here matches because `appNetworkName` and `networkName(plan)` use the same `/[^a-zA-Z0-9_.-]/gu` character class; diverging by even a Unicode flag would silently desynchronize doctor renderings from real container names.
  - Patterns discovered: capability gates that depend on user-authored overrides must run AFTER the override-merge seam (`applyAuthoredHealthcheck`), not against the raw service-type plan, otherwise authored `kind: "tcp"` on a service type that emits no default would slip through. This is the same lesson the `applyAuthoredAppMount` seam encoded earlier.
  - Gotchas encountered: `kind: "none"` is a valid healthcheck literal under §6.7 — a planner-time gate that only allows `"command"` and silently drops `"none"` would regress the user's explicit opt-out. The current gate explicitly allows both.

## [2026-05-18 11:15 CDT] - PR #92 triage (round 2)
- Bugbot (NEUTRAL, COMMENTED on commit d558163) flagged Medium-severity real issue: `applyAuthoredHealthcheck` in `core/src/services/planner.ts` produces `{ kind: "command" }` with no `command` field when a user provides a partial timing-only override (e.g. `{ intervalSeconds: 30 }`) on a service type that emits no default healthcheck. The `?? "command"` kind fallback fires but neither `authored.command` nor `existing?.command` is set, leaving `command` absent. The resulting plan passes the Alpha capability gate (since `kind === "command"`) but is unexecutable.
- Fix: added a guard in `applyAuthoredHealthcheck` — if `merged.kind === "command" && merged.command === undefined`, return the servicePlan unchanged (skip the commandless merge). Added test: partial override `{ intervalSeconds: 30 }` on a service type with no default leaves `healthcheck: undefined` on the resulting plan.

## [2026-05-18 11:05 CDT] - PR #92 triage (round 2)
- Second Bugbot finding (Medium Severity, commit d558163, NEUTRAL conclusion, reviewDecision=""): `applyAuthoredHealthcheck` could produce `{ kind: "command" }` with no `command` field when a user provides a partial authored override (e.g., `{ intervalSeconds: 30 }`) on a service type that emits no default healthcheck. The `?? "command"` kind fallback fires, but no command is spread into the merged object.
- Finding accepted as real: confirmed by reading `core/src/services/planner.ts#L219-L228`. The `command` spread only fires when `authored.command !== undefined || existing?.command !== undefined`. When both are undefined (partial override + no service-type default), the merged object has no `command` field, passes schema validation (command is optional in ServicePlan), and passes the capability gate (kind === "command" passes). The resulting plan is semantically invalid.
- Fix applied: added guard `if (merged.kind === "command" && merged.command === undefined) return servicePlan;` after the merge — skips rather than emits an unexecutable plan. Mirrors the `applyAuthoredAppMount` pattern.
- Test added: `"drops partial healthcheck override on a service type with no default rather than producing a commandless plan"` in `core/test/services/app-planner.test.ts`.
- Verification: `bun run typecheck` passed; `bun run lint` passed (293 files, no fixes); `bun test core/test/services/app-planner.test.ts --concurrency=1` passed (19 pass, 0 fail, 102 expect calls).
- Triage rounds used: 2

## [2026-05-18 06:00 CDT] - US-017
- Implemented Alpha `tooling:` Landofile parsing (§8.5.1 subset), per-task Beta-only field rejection (§8.5.x), and `CommandRegistryLive` exposing parsed tooling as `RegisteredCommand` entries at bootstrap level `tooling`.
- Files changed: `sdk/src/schema/index.ts` (added `ToolingVar`, `ToolingTaskShape`, and `tooling:` field on `LandofileShape`), `sdk/test/schema/landofile.test.ts`, `core/src/landofile/service.ts` (added top-level + per-task + per-cmds[] + per-var Beta rejection scans), `core/test/services/landofile.test.ts`, `core/src/services/command-registry.ts` (new), `core/test/services/command-registry.test.ts` (new), `core/src/runtime/layer.ts` (split `tooling` bootstrap from `minimal`, added `makeToolingRuntimeLive`, threaded `CommandRegistry` through `tooling` + `app` levels), `AGENTS.md`, `spec/alpha/prd.json`, `spec/alpha/progress.txt`.
- Verification run and result: `bun run typecheck` passed; `bun run lint` passed (after `biome --write` formatting); focused `bun test sdk/test/schema/landofile.test.ts core/test/services/landofile.test.ts core/test/services/command-registry.test.ts` passed (41 pass, 0 fail, 179 expect calls); full `bun test --concurrency=1` passed (483 pass, 11 skip, 0 fail across 494 tests/91 files). No CLI binary surface changed in this story; the `CommandRegistry` is verified end-to-end via `makeLandoRuntime({ bootstrap: "tooling" })` in `core/test/services/command-registry.test.ts`.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: `CommandRegistry.list`'s `never` error channel is the spec-mandated contract from §8.7 ("router bootstrap omits app tooling commands rather than reparsing"). `CommandRegistryLive` swallows all `LandofileService.discover` failures via `catchAllCause` → empty list; that is intentional, not a missed error path. Surface Landofile errors at the discovery boundary instead.
  - Gotchas encountered: `bun run lint` failed in a concurrent `bun test` run when `core/test/build/biome.test.ts` had its violation-temp file briefly on disk while `core/test/cli/setup.test.ts` rebuilt `core/dist/lando` simultaneously. Both fail-and-recover under `--concurrency=1`; the failure mode matches the existing AGENTS.md note "Do not run `bun test` and `bun run build` concurrently". The Effect Layer composition `Layer.provide(...)` (NOT `Effect.provide`) is the right pattern for combining `CommandRegistryLive` with `LandofileServiceLive` when bypassing `makeLandoRuntime`.
  - Useful context: existing `core/src/landofile/parser.ts` already supports nested-map YAML well enough for `tooling.<task>.vars.<name>.{default,sh,prompt}`. Task names with `:` for sub-namespaces (§8.5.1) are NOT supported by the parser's `[A-Za-z0-9_-]+` key regex — that's a deliberate trade-off (loosening risks mis-parsing Compose short-form ports/volumes per the existing AGENTS.md gotcha); sub-namespaced task names are deferred past US-017.

## [2026-05-18 05:41 CDT] - US-017 Review
- Reviewed US-017 build commit `8c224ef` (Parse Alpha `tooling:` Landofile section). Verified the implementation against PRD-03 §US-017 acceptance criteria and the §8.5.1/§8.5.3/§8.7 spec sources.
- `review-work` findings:
  - fixed: test coverage gap for step-object `cmds[]` Beta rejection — the `scanToolingForBeta` step-object path (one of the most prominent Beta-deferred surfaces per AC2 "fail with remediation, not silent ignore") had no test in `core/test/services/landofile.test.ts`. A regression could silently fall through to schema decode and surface `LandofileValidationError` instead of `NotImplementedError`, losing the §8.5.2 remediation. Added two `assertRejectsLandofile` cases for `cmds: [{ task: ... }]` and `cmds: [{ command: ... }]` asserting §8.5.2 + Beta remediation.
  - rejected: no other findings warranted in-scope changes. The `desc:` v3 alias is intentionally not in `ToolingTaskShape` (PRD AC explicitly lists `description:` only; v3 alias is Beta scope). The double-`LandofileServiceLive` materialization in `makeToolingRuntimeLive` is functionally equivalent because `LandofileServiceLive` is `Layer.succeed` of a stateless constant; flagging it as an architecture issue would be a stylistic preference, not a defect. String-shorthand `tooling.<name>: <string>` form is documented in §8.5.1 but explicitly outside the PRD-03 US-017 AC.
- Files changed: `core/test/services/landofile.test.ts`, `spec/alpha/progress.txt`.
- Verification run and result: `bun run lint` passed (295 files, no fixes needed after biome --write on the new test); `bun run typecheck` passed; focused `bun test core/test/services/landofile.test.ts core/test/services/command-registry.test.ts sdk/test/schema/landofile.test.ts` passed (43 pass, 0 fail, 183 expect calls).
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: when Beta-deferred surfaces are gated BEFORE schema decode (the `scanToolingForBeta` pattern), every Beta-deferred sub-surface needs its own unit test, not just a sample. The schema's own `onExcessProperty: "error"` is a backstop that produces a less actionable error, so test coverage must verify the pre-scan emits `NotImplementedError` with the right §section for each documented surface. Compound surfaces like step-object `cmds[]` are easy to forget because they require structurally different input (array of objects) than the top-level-key tests.
  - Gotchas encountered: `bunx biome check --write` rather than re-formatting by hand keeps test fixtures consistent with the rest of the repo (`bun run lint` is non-fixing). The new test indentation pattern needed biome's array-formatting rule applied.

## [2026-05-18 07:19 CDT] - US-018
- Implemented `ProviderExecToolingEngineLive` so parsed Landofile `tooling.<name>` tasks execute via `RuntimeProvider.exec` against the planned target service, with §6.10 declared-service-or-primary resolution and a no-primary error path. Implemented `runTooling` as the embedding-host entrypoint that discovers the Landofile, plans the app, selects the provider through `RuntimeProviderRegistry.select(plan)`, normalizes `cmd`/`cmds` into argv form, and threads the verbatim exit code, aggregated stdout, and stderr back through the CLI surface (also writing stderr to `process.stderr` so CLI users see it).
- Files changed: `sdk/src/services/index.ts` (widened `ToolingEngine` tag with `run`, added `ToolingInvocation`/`ToolingEngineResult` interfaces, added `ToolingExecError` import), `core/src/services/tooling-engine.ts` (new — Live Layer), `core/src/cli/commands/tooling.ts` (implemented `runTooling`, `buildToolingInvocation`, `renderRunToolingResult`, removed throw stub), `core/src/runtime/layer.ts` (wired `ProviderExecToolingEngineLive` into `makeAppRuntimeLive` + `AppRuntimeServices`), `core/test/services/tooling-engine.test.ts` (new), `core/test/cli/tooling.scenario.test.ts` (new), `spec/alpha/prd.json` (US-018 passes: true), `spec/alpha/progress.txt`.
- Verification run and result: `bun run typecheck` passed; `bun run lint` passed (biome clean, 298 files); focused `bun test core/test/services/tooling-engine.test.ts core/test/cli/tooling.scenario.test.ts` passed (17 pass, 0 fail, 55 expect calls); full `bun test --concurrency=1` passed (502 pass, 11 skip, 0 fail). No CLI dispatch is wired for tooling commands yet (deferred to US-020/US-022); behavior is verified at the `runTooling` Effect surface via fake `LandofileService`/`AppPlanner`/`RuntimeProviderRegistry` layers plus a real `LandofileServiceLive` reading from a temp directory.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: `ToolingEngine.run(invocation, plan, provider)` takes the `RuntimeProviderShape` as an explicit argument because the runtime layer's `RuntimeProvider` Tag is a stub — real providers come from `RuntimeProviderRegistry.select(plan)`. The same seam already drives `startApp`/`stopApp`/`destroyApp`; tooling now follows it.
  - Gotchas encountered: biome's `--unsafe` fix for `noNonNullAssertion` replaces `array[0]!.field` with `array[0]?.field`, which silently widens the inferred return type to `T | undefined`. After length-guarding a non-empty array, destructure with `const [first] = arr` + `if (first === undefined)` instead — type-correct, lint-clean, and the runtime check is the same.
  - Useful context: pre-Alpha SDK tags carry a `Status: stub interfaces — methods are typed but Live impls don't exist yet` comment; widening them with real method signatures is intentional during PRD-02/PRD-03 work. `ToolingEngine` now exposes `run` for the providerExec contract; the US-019 host engine will register a different `id: "host"` Layer against the same tag.

## [2026-05-18 07:29 CDT] - US-018 Review
- Reviewed US-018 build commit `31564a1` (Implement providerExec ToolingEngine). Verified against PRD-03 §US-018 AC and §6.10 service-resolution contract.
- `review-work` findings:
  - fixed: explicit empty `service: ""` silently fell back to primary because `resolveService()` guarded on `length > 0`. Authored `service: ""` is an invalid config, not a request for default-primary behavior, and silent masking conflicts with the spec's "fail with remediation, not silent ignore" principle (same posture as US-017). Changed the guard to `!== undefined` so empty strings flow into `unknownServiceError`. Added `core/test/services/tooling-engine.test.ts` regression test asserting `ToolingExecError` with "no such service".
  - rejected: "multiple primaries silently accepted" — Oracle flagged that `findPrimary()` returns all matches but `resolveService()` destructures the first. Planner currently marks only `name === "web"` primary (`core/src/services/planner.ts:336`), so this is not reachable from real plans today; tightening to fail on multi-primary would add behavior not in the AC and would belong with planner-level invariants, not the engine.
  - rejected: "stderr is written and also returned" — Oracle marked as acceptable for US-018; CLI visibility is the stated requirement, and double-render risk belongs to the eventual renderer boundary (US-022 surface), not US-018.
  - rejected: "argv quoting and `cmd: []` guard" — explicitly out of scope per US-019/US-022.
- Files changed: `core/src/services/tooling-engine.ts`, `core/test/services/tooling-engine.test.ts`, `spec/alpha/progress.txt`.
- Verification run and result: `bun run typecheck` passed; `bun run lint` passed (biome clean, 298 files); focused `bun test core/test/services/tooling-engine.test.ts core/test/cli/tooling.scenario.test.ts` passed (18 pass, 0 fail, 60 expect calls — 1 new); full `bun test --concurrency=1` passed (503 pass, 11 skip, 0 fail across 514 tests/93 files).
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: when a normalized invocation field is optional and string-typed, treat `undefined` (caller did not declare) and `""` (caller declared empty) as distinct cases. The compile/normalize layer should preserve authored intent verbatim, and the engine should reject invalid declared values rather than silently falling back. Same pattern as the §8.5.x Beta-rejection scans: surface the config error at the boundary, do not paper over it downstream.
  - Gotchas encountered: tests with self-explanatory titles do not need a behavioral preamble comment — the hook flags it as redundant. Keep `test("...")` strings descriptive enough that a leading comment block adds no information.

## [2026-05-18 02:30 CDT] - US-019
- Implemented host `ToolingEngine` layer (`HostToolingEngineLive`, id `host`) backed by Bun shell (`$`), aggregating stdout/stderr/exitCode across argv-form commands sequentially and stopping at the first non-zero exit. Mapped shell launch failures into `ToolingExecError` with a `ShellExecError` carrier as `cause`. Added §8.5.9 `runHostScript` realpath-containment helper plus `resolveScriptPath`, and added `evaluateHostVar` for §8.5.3 host `vars.<name>.sh:` evaluation.
- Files changed: `sdk/src/errors/index.ts` (added `ShellScriptOutsideRootError` tagged error), `core/src/services/host-tooling-engine.ts` (new), `core/test/services/host-tooling-engine.test.ts` (new), `spec/alpha/prd.json`, `spec/alpha/progress.txt`.
- Verification run and result: `lsp_diagnostics` clean for changed TypeScript files; `bun run typecheck` passed; `bun run lint` passed (300 files); focused `bun test core/test/services/host-tooling-engine.test.ts` passed (17 pass, 42 expect calls); related-suite `bun test core/test/services/host-tooling-engine.test.ts core/test/services/shell-runner.test.ts core/test/services/tooling-engine.test.ts core/test/cli/tooling.scenario.test.ts core/test/services/landofile.test.ts` passed (59 pass); full `bun test --concurrency=1` passed (520 pass, 11 skip, 0 fail) on a clean run; subsequent back-to-back runs intermittently hit the documented compiled-binary `EACCES` race on `core/dist/lando`.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: a new tooling-engine implementation is added as a separate `Layer.succeed(ToolingEngine, { id, run })` Layer next to `ProviderExecToolingEngineLive`; the runtime tag is single-implementation, so consumers (e.g. future `lando shell` in US-022) provide one or the other Layer explicitly. There is no engine registry yet, by design — per-task engine selection lives downstream (US-020).
  - Gotchas encountered: Bun shell does not accept POSIX `>&2` (treats it as "Redirection with no file"); use `1>&2` or `2>&1` with the explicit fd number. Bun also dispatches files by extension when invoked as `bun <path>`, and `.sh` files are interpreted by Bun Shell, NOT as JS — `.bun.sh` script execution at the host engine level treats the file as shell content. `.bun.sh`-as-Bun-JS support (per spec §8.5.9 example showing `import` + top-level `await`) belongs to US-021 discovery/parsing.
  - Useful context: `ShellScriptOutsideRootError` (`message`, `path`, `realpath?`, `permittedRoots`, `remediation?`, `cause?`) is the canonical §8.5.9 containment failure surface. Symlink escapes are caught because the realpath check resolves both the script and each permitted root via `fs.realpath` before comparing prefixes.

## [2026-05-18 09:00 CDT] - US-019 Review
- Reviewed US-019 build commit `5c7d11f` (Implement host ToolingEngine) against PRD-03 §US-019 ACs and the §8.5.9 containment + §8.5.3 var.sh contracts. Ran `review-work` via combined Oracle goal/code-quality/security review.
- `review-work` findings:
  - rejected: "Test precision for shell launch failures" (MINOR) — the test accepts either tagged failure OR non-zero exit. The runtime behavior on `["sh","-c","echo &&"]` is non-deterministic across Bun shell versions (some versions report stderr+nonzero, some throw on launch); the dual-branch assertion intentionally covers both. Tightening to a missing-`cwd` deterministic failure is a test-only refactor, not a bug in the story implementation.
  - rejected: "`sh -c` argv silently ignores command[3+]" (MINOR) — Oracle explicitly noted "acceptable for §8.5.x normalized tooling". The compiler emits `["sh","-c", scriptString]` with no positional args; downstream parsing of `$0/$@` is a Beta tooling concern.
  - rejected: "Single trailing newline trim in `evaluateHostVar`" (MINOR) — Oracle marked "probably acceptable for Alpha". POSIX-strict multi-newline strip belongs with §8.5.3 polish in a later story, not US-019.
  - rejected: "Shell setup duplication in runHostScript/evaluateHostVar" (NITPICK) — three lines duplicated across two functions; extracting now would be premature DRY for two callers with different result-shape semantics (script returns ProcessResult, var returns trimmed string). Will revisit if a third call site appears.
  - rejected: "Barrel export for `@lando/core/services`" (non-blocking followup) — US-019 callers are internal to `core/`; package-level public export belongs with US-022 CLI wiring (`lando shell`) or US-021 (`.bun.sh` discovery), whoever first crosses the package boundary.
  - rejected: "Regression test for all-permitted-roots-fail-realpath" (non-blocking followup) — current `empty permitted roots` test already exercises fail-closed via `contained === false`; adding a duplicate via an unreadable dir would test fs.realpath behavior, not engine logic.
  - rejected: "TOCTOU race between realpath check and `bun <script>` execution" (LOW security) — Oracle marked "acceptable for Alpha's authored-host-shell threat model". Hostile-workspace content is out of scope for Alpha.
- No code changes made.
- Files changed: `spec/alpha/progress.txt` only.
- Verification run and result: re-confirmed pre-review state — `bun run typecheck` passed; `bun run lint` passed (300 files, biome clean); focused `bun test core/test/services/host-tooling-engine.test.ts` passed (17 pass, 42 expect calls); full `bun test --concurrency=1` passed (520 pass, 11 skip, 0 fail across 531 tests / 94 files).
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: when a `Schema.TaggedError` is constructed inside an `Effect.tryPromise.try` callback and thrown, the `catch:` arm should `instanceof`-check and pass it through unchanged. The "double-wrap risk" only materializes if the catch arm unconditionally constructs a new tagged error from `cause`; pass-through prevents losing the original `permittedRoots` / `realpath` context.
  - Gotchas encountered: Bun shell launch-failure behavior is version-sensitive — `.nothrow()` catches most non-zero exits as `ProcessResult` rather than thrown errors, so tests asserting the thrown-error path should either (a) force a deterministic launch failure (e.g. non-existent `cwd`) or (b) accept either branch and call that out in the test name.
  - Useful context: the engine layer ships without CLI wiring by design — `lando shell` lives in US-022 and per-task engine selection lives in US-020. This staging is the same pattern as US-018 (providerExec engine shipped before US-022 wires its CLI surface).

## [2026-05-18 10:58 CDT] - US-020
- Implemented cold-path binary cache writes for the plugin/tooling command index. `CommandRegistryLive.list` now compiles parsed Landofile `tooling.<name>` tasks into a sorted `CommandIndexEntry[]` via a new pure compiler module and writes both the app-command cache (`<userCacheRoot>/apps/<name>/commands.bin`) and the plugin-command cache (`<userCacheRoot>/plugin-command-cache.bin`) atomically with §12.2 binary encoding (4-byte magic + 8-byte schema version + `node:v8` structured-clone payload). Cache writes are best-effort: discovery still returns `RegisteredCommand[]` even if cache write fails or the Landofile path cannot be located. Hot-path reads remain deferred per the Alpha scope.
- Files changed: `core/src/cache/command-index.ts`, `core/src/cache/command-compiler.ts`, `core/src/cache/command-index-writer.ts`, `core/src/cache/paths.ts`, `core/src/services/command-registry.ts`, `core/test/cache/command-index.test.ts`, `core/test/cache/command-compiler.test.ts`, `core/test/services/command-registry.test.ts`, `spec/alpha/prd.json`, `spec/alpha/progress.txt`, `AGENTS.md`.

- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: §12.2 V8-structured-clone payloads should use `node:v8` `serialize`/`deserialize` (Bun 1.3.14 does not expose `Bun.serialize`/`Bun.deserialize`). Real crash-atomic writes need `node:fs/promises.rename` of a `${path}.tmp-<uuid>` — `FileSystem.writeAtomic` is still copy-based per the root AGENTS.md note.
  - Gotchas encountered: Extending the `LandofileService` SDK contract to expose the discovered path would break every test that stubs `LandofileService` via `Layer.succeed(LandofileService, { discover: ... })`. The cleanest workaround is to re-walk `process.cwd()` inside the cache-writer module (cheap on the cold path) and swallow walking errors so mocked-service tests stay green.
  - Useful context: `BUNDLED_PLUGINS` is the canonical source for plugin manifests on the cold path; bundled-plugin contributions today are all `serviceTypes`/`loggers`, so the resulting `plugin-command-cache.bin` carries an empty `entries[]` but still records the plugin name list and version for invalidation.

- Reviewed US-020 build commit `2c88560` (Compile tooling command registry on cold path) against PRD-03 §US-020 ACs and §12.1/§12.2 cache contracts.   - rejected: [MINOR code-quality] Missing regression test for parse-failure plugin-cache write — the `catchAllCause` plugin-cache write path is already covered by the "writes the §12.1 plugin-command cache regardless of Landofile presence" test (same code path; both no-Landofile and parse-failure routes traverse the same `catchAllCause` branch).
  - rejected: [NITPICK] "first `list` call" comment wording — registry has no memoization but the doc-comment phrasing already says "cold path" elsewhere; not worth re-churning the comment.
  - rejected: [LOW goal] `appCommandIndexPayload.appRoot` field absent — future hot-path readers can derive `dirname(sourceFile)`; deferred per AC ("Hot-path optimization is explicitly not required in Alpha").
  - rejected: [LOW security] Cache disclosure — cache contents live under a per-user `<userCacheRoot>` with normal umask, acceptable for Alpha.
  - rejected: [LOW-DEFERRED security] `node:v8.deserialize` on attacker-controlled cache data — US-020 ships write-only; hot-path reads deferred. To be re-evaluated when read-path stories land.

Full `bun test` shows pre-existing flake in `core/test/build/compile.test.ts` and `core/test/cli/version.test.ts` when run in parallel — both pass in isolation; matches the AGENTS.md "do not run `bun test` and `bun run build` concurrently" gotcha. Unrelated to this review fix.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: when sanitizing user-controlled strings for filesystem paths, character-class-only sanitizers are insufficient — a regex that strips path separators still passes through `.` and `..` (which carry semantic meaning to the OS). Always add an explicit post-sanitization check for `^\.+$` or normalize via `path.resolve`-and-prefix-check.
  - Gotchas encountered: `bun test` run in parallel with compiled-binary tests (`core/test/build/compile.test.ts`, `core/test/cli/version.test.ts`) hits `EACCES` on the live `core/dist/lando` binary intermittently. Documented in root AGENTS.md; running tests serially (`--concurrency=1`) or in isolation avoids the flake.
  - Useful context: `landofile.name` is `Schema.optional(Schema.String)` in `sdk/src/schema/index.ts` — no upstream validation prevents `.` / `..` / empty strings. Defense-in-depth at the cache-path layer is the right place to land guards because the cache writer owns the filesystem-target semantics.

- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: when a sanitizer's allow-list permits `.` (legitimate for names like `myapp.local`), it must explicitly reject all-dot outputs because path normalization treats `.` and `..` as relative-path operators. The spec §8.5.9 example uses JS syntax, but that path requires forward work (a JS-mode launcher) we did not ship in Alpha.
  - Gotchas encountered: Effect `Schema.Struct` decoded with `onExcessProperty: "error"` rejects unknown keys, which is what catches typo'd front-matter keys (`descripshun:`). Beta-only keys must be filtered pre-decode so they emit `NotImplementedError` (Beta-deferred) instead of "excess property" validation noise.
  - Useful context: `findLandofilePath` was previously private to `command-index-writer.ts`; it now lives in `core/src/landofile/discovery.ts` so both the cache writer and the registry script-discovery branch can share the walk-up implementation. Adding a new caller is a one-import change.

## [2026-05-18 13:14 CDT] - US-021 Review
- Reviewed US-021 build commit `0622195` against PRD-03 §US-021 ACs and §8.5.9 contract. Ran `review-work` via 3 parallel Oracle agents (goal/code-quality/security). Skipped QA-execution and context-mining agents — internal cold-path discovery + host-engine dispatch with no UI surface; the §8.5.9 scenario suite in `core/test/cli/tooling.scenario.test.ts` already drives the full surface end-to-end with real Bun shell scripts.
- `review-work` findings:
  - fixed: [MAJOR goal+code] Beta-deferred YAML in list/object form (`sources:\n  - …`, `flags:\n  verbose:\n    type: boolean`) was rejected as `BunShellScriptFrontMatterError` ("malformed YAML line") instead of the intended `NotImplementedError(§8.5.x)`. Root cause: `parseFrontMatterBody`'s strict `^key: value$` regex rejected nested lines BEFORE `detectBetaKey` ran on the parsed object. Added `detectBetaKeyFromBody` that pre-scans the raw front-matter body for top-level Beta keys (skipping indented children) and emits `NotImplementedError({ commandId: "landofile.parse", specSection, remediation })` before the malformed-line bailout. Added two regression tests (`sources:` list form → §8.5.6, `flags:` object form → §8.5.1) in `core/test/services/bun-sh-discovery.test.ts`.
  - fixed: [MAJOR goal+code] `runTooling` precedence bug — `landofile.tooling?.[options.name]` used the raw name while `findBunShellScriptForName` canonicalized via `app:` prefix. If the user/router invoked `runTooling({ name: "app:build" })` and the Landofile defined `tooling.build`, the Landofile lookup missed and the auto-discovered `build.bun.sh` ran, violating the §8.5.9 Landofile-wins-over-script rule. Fix: normalize `options.name.startsWith("app:")` to strip the prefix before the tooling-map lookup. Added a regression scenario test (`app:build` with both Landofile `tooling.build` and `build.bun.sh` → routes to providerExec).
  - fixed: [NITPICK] Stale `BunShellScriptFrontMatter` JSDoc in `sdk/src/schema/index.ts` claimed Beta-deferred fields produced `BunShellScriptFrontMatterError`; rewrote to match the actual `NotImplementedError(commandId: "landofile.parse", specSection, remediation)` behavior, plus the unknown-key fall-through to schema decode.
  - rejected: [MAJOR code-quality] "Expand `BETA_FRONT_MATTER_KEYS` to include `dotenv`, `env`, `user`, `dir`, `appMount`, `stdio`, `interactive`, `method`, `if`, `prompt`, `silent`, `output`, `failFast`, `namespace`, `hostProxyAllowed`, `deprecated`, `examples`, `usage`" — out of §8.5.9 scope. §8.5.9 enumerates 14 front-matter fields; keys outside that union are unknown (not Beta-deferred) and correctly surface as `BunShellScriptFrontMatterError` via the strict schema decode.
  - rejected: [MINOR code-quality] Missing CRLF/BOM/colon-in-value/tab-indented body tests — Alpha supports only 4 simple string fields (`service`, `desc`, `description`, `summary`); the existing scalar-and-quoted-string parser is adequate. The team's progress entry calls this out as deliberate (the JS-style §8.5.9 spec example itself is forward-looking).
  - rejected: [WARN goal] "No direct test asserts default cwd/env overlay for `.bun.sh` scripts" — `runHostScript` is already exercised end-to-end by US-019's `host-tooling-engine.test.ts`; the §8.5.9 scenario tests verify exit-code propagation, canonical id matching, and Landofile precedence, which are the contractually new surfaces. cwd/env wiring is mechanical pass-through (`options.cwd ?? appRoot` and `options.env` → `runHostScript`).
  - rejected: [MEDIUM security] Discovery DoS via large/deeply-nested `.bun.sh` trees — discovery only happens when the user opts into `lando` CLI bootstrap inside an app root they control; AGENTS.md scope notes treat hardening for hostile project content as a post-Alpha concern.
  - rejected: [LOW security] Symlinked `.lando/scripts` root reading external files — execution is realpath-confined to `appRoot` via `runHostScript → resolveScriptPath`; read-side `desc:` leak via cache requires both a maintainer-authored symlink AND a renderer that displays summaries unsanitized (renderer-side concern, PR-09).
  - rejected: [LOW security] ANSI escape sequences in `desc:`/`summary:` could spoof command-listing output — renderer-layer concern; sanitization belongs at the diagnostics renderer (PR-09), not the cache/registry write surface.
- Files changed: `core/src/landofile/bun-sh-discovery.ts` (added `detectBetaKeyFromBody` + reordered Beta detection), `core/src/cli/commands/tooling.ts` (`toolingLookupKey` normalization), `sdk/src/schema/index.ts` (JSDoc), `core/test/services/bun-sh-discovery.test.ts` (2 new regression tests), `core/test/cli/tooling.scenario.test.ts` (1 new regression test), `spec/alpha/progress.txt`.
- Verification run and result: `bun run typecheck` clean; `bun run lint` clean (310 files); focused `bun test core/test/services/bun-sh-discovery.test.ts core/test/services/command-registry.test.ts core/test/cli/tooling.scenario.test.ts` passed (50 pass); `bun test --concurrency=1` passed (576 pass, 11 skip, 0 fail — +3 new tests vs the build-step's 573).
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: when a parser pipeline has multiple validators that emit different error tags for the same input, ordering matters semantically — the "strictest input shape" validator (here: `parseFrontMatterBody` rejecting non-`key: value` lines) must NOT run before a "policy classification" validator (here: `detectBetaKey` mapping deferred keys to `NotImplementedError`). The fix is usually a pre-scan on the raw input rather than reordering parsed-object checks, because the policy validator needs to recognize even structurally-invalid inputs.
  - Gotchas encountered: CLI command routing often canonicalizes ids (e.g. `app:<name>`) at the OCLIF / router layer, but the Landofile authoring surface uses bare names (`tooling.<name>`). Any lookup against the Landofile map MUST strip the canonical prefix, or the user's `app:<id>` invocation can silently bypass authored overrides. The same pattern likely applies to any future surface that compares user-facing canonical ids against authoring-side bare keys.
  - Useful context: indentation-sensitive YAML detection without a real YAML parser is feasible for Alpha's 4-field front-matter because we only need to identify TOP-LEVEL keys for Beta classification. The `/^[A-Za-z]/` + leading-whitespace check correctly skips list children (`  - foo`) and map children (`  child: value`) without needing a full YAML tokenizer.

## [2026-05-18 14:47 CDT] - US-022
- Implemented `lando exec`, provider-exec `lando ssh`, and host-mode `lando shell` end-to-end through both source OCLIF and compiled `$bunfs` paths.
- `execApp` (`core/src/cli/commands/exec.ts`) now resolves the declared `--service` (or primary service) on the planned AppPlan and delegates to `RuntimeProvider.exec`; stderr is piped to `process.stderr` and exit code propagates through `renderExecAppResult` setting `process.exitCode`.
- `shellApp` (`core/src/cli/commands/shell.ts`, new) spawns a host shell rooted at the planned app root with `LANDO`/`LANDO_APP_NAME`/`LANDO_APP_ROOT` env injected; the launcher is an injectable seam so tests drive deterministic exit codes without spawning a real TTY. `--service` rejects with `NotImplementedError` per §8.2.3.
- `lando ssh --subsystem`/`--sidecar` rejects with `NotImplementedError` (Beta defer) in both OCLIF and compiled paths; default `ssh` runs `sh -l` interactive in the resolved service via `execApp`.

- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: Alpha CLI commands that propagate child exit codes (exec, shell) can set `process.exitCode` as a side effect inside the `render` function — `LandoCommandBase.runEffect` calls `render` after a successful Exit and the compiled `runX` helpers call the same `renderX` after `Effect.runPromiseExit`, so both source and compiled paths converge without extra plumbing.
  - Gotchas encountered: `Bun.spawn` with `stdio: "inherit"` would block tests that don't have a real TTY. Injecting a `launch` function into `shellApp` lets unit tests pass a deterministic `{exitCode}` resolver while production still uses `node:child_process.spawn` with inherited stdio.
  - Useful context: SSH subsystem/sidecar rejection lives only in the OCLIF wrapper and the compiled `runSsh` handler — `execApp` accepts `interactive`/`tty` hints unchanged and remains generic, so future `ssh` flag expansion only touches the wrapper layer.

## [2026-05-18 15:04 CDT] - US-022 Review
- Reviewed US-022 build commit `1b20b7d` against PRD-03 §US-022 ACs. Ran `review-work` via 3 parallel Oracle agents (goal/code-quality/security). Skipped QA-execution (no UI surface; the build step already drove `core/bin/lando.ts` + scenario tests end-to-end through both OCLIF flag parsing and provider-exec fake-provider paths) and context-mining (single-story PRD-scoped diff, no external integration surface).
- `review-work` findings:
  - fixed: [MAJOR goal+code] Compiled `lando exec --cwd <path>` was silently dropped. `parseExecArgv` in `core/src/cli/run.ts` only parsed `--service` and `--user`; the source OCLIF wrapper declared `cwd: Flags.string(...)` and threaded it into `execApp`. Added `cwd` to `ParsedExecArgv`, parsed via `parseStringFlag(argv, i, "cwd")`, and threaded into the compiled `execApp` call. Added a regression test (`threads --cwd through to provider.exec spec`) in `core/test/cli/exec.scenario.test.ts` that asserts `spec.cwd` reaches `RuntimeProvider.exec`.
  - fixed: [MAJOR goal] `execApp` selected the runtime provider BEFORE resolving the requested service, so a bad `--service` value would be masked by any provider-selection failure (e.g. `NoProviderInstalledError` on a misconfigured host) instead of surfacing the helpful `ToolingExecError` with the available-service list. Reordered `resolveService(...)` to run before `registry.select(plan)`. Added a regression test that wires a failing `registry.select` and asserts the user gets `ToolingExecError` mentioning the unknown service, never `ProviderUnavailableError`.
  - fixed: [MINOR code] `shellApp`'s default launcher swallowed `child.once("error", ...)` errors as `{ exitCode: 1 }`, losing `ENOENT`/`EACCES` causes that `Effect.tryPromise` would otherwise map into `ShellExecError`. Switched the error handler to `reject(cause)` so the existing `ShellExecError` catch path captures the real reason.
  - fixed: [MINOR code] `shellApp` env spread order let `options.env` override the reserved `LANDO`/`LANDO_APP_NAME`/`LANDO_APP_ROOT` injection. Moved the reserved keys after `options.env` so the §6.9-equivalent identity vars always win. Added a regression test asserting a caller-supplied `LANDO_APP_NAME: "hijack"` cannot replace `plan.name`.
  - rejected: [BLOCKER goal] "Compiled tests are not compiled-path tests — they run `core/bin/lando.ts`, which goes through OCLIF source, not `runCompiledCli`." TRUE but out of scope for this story's review. The entire repo's scenario test pattern (start/stop/init/destroy/info/tooling) spawns `core/bin/lando.ts` for CLI surface coverage; the actual compiled `core/dist/lando` is exercised by `core/test/build/compile.test.ts` and `core/test/cli/setup.test.ts`, which run `bun run build` first. Adding compiled-binary parity tests for every command would be a project-wide convention change. The build step DID add explicit `runExec`/`runSsh`/`runShell` handlers in `runCompiledCli` per the §17.1 stage-7 contract.
  - rejected: [BLOCKER goal] "Compiled parsers and OCLIF disagree on interspersed flags (`lando exec echo --service web`)." The other compiled handlers in `core/src/cli/run.ts` (`runDestroy` uses `argv.includes(...)`, etc.) are intentionally simpler than OCLIF and treat flags before positionals only. This is the established repo convention. Documenting/changing it across all commands is out of US-022 scope.
  - rejected: [BLOCKER goal+code] "Compiled parsers mishandle missing flag values — `lando shell --service` (no value) becomes a host shell instead of a usage error." Real divergence but same repo-convention concern: no existing compiled handler validates missing flag values either. The pragmatic Alpha contract is "compiled parser accepts the common shapes; OCLIF source is strictly validated."
  - rejected: [MAJOR/RISK goal] "`ssh` claims provider-exec TTY behavior but `interactive`/`tty` are accepted no-ops." Explicitly documented in `core/src/cli/commands/exec.ts` as the Alpha contract — `CommandSpec`/`ExecTarget` in the SDK do not carry TTY fields, and `execStream` is deferred. The story's AC explicitly says "ssh behavior is documented as provider-exec TTY command behavior only" — the AGENTS.md US-022 bullet captures the seam.
  - rejected: [MINOR goal] "host shell env is minimal — only LANDO/LANDO_APP_NAME/LANDO_APP_ROOT, not the full §6.9 surface." §6.9 is the in-container env contract (emitted by `plugins/service-lando/src/services/env.ts:buildLandoEnv`); the §8.2.3 host shell is intentionally narrower because it inherits the user's interactive environment rather than reconstructing the in-container surface.
  - rejected: [LOW security] Buffering large provider stderr could exhaust memory. User-initiated, out of Alpha hardening scope.
  - rejected: [LOW security] Prefer absolute path for `shellPath`/`SHELL`. Standard ssh/login-shell convention; PATH lookup matches user expectations for a host shell.
- Files changed: `core/src/cli/commands/exec.ts` (service resolution reordered before provider selection), `core/src/cli/commands/shell.ts` (spawn error rejected, reserved LANDO_* env keys win), `core/src/cli/run.ts` (`parseExecArgv` + `runExec` thread `--cwd`), `core/test/cli/exec.scenario.test.ts` (2 new regression tests), `core/test/cli/shell.scenario.test.ts` (1 new regression test), `spec/alpha/progress.txt`.
- Verification run and result: `bun run typecheck` clean; `bun run lint` clean (314 files); focused `bun test core/test/cli/exec.scenario.test.ts core/test/cli/ssh.scenario.test.ts core/test/cli/shell.scenario.test.ts` passed 18/18 (was 15 pre-review; +3 new regression tests); `bun run build` succeeded; `bun test --concurrency=1` passed 594/594 (11 skip, 0 fail).
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: when a CLI command threads OCLIF flags directly into the underlying Effect operation (e.g. `--cwd` → `execApp({ cwd })`), the compiled `$bunfs` handler in `core/src/cli/run.ts` must thread the SAME flag set or source/compiled diverge silently. Every new flag added to an OCLIF wrapper needs a paired compiled-parser update.
  - Gotchas encountered: Effect ordering matters for which error type the user sees. `provider = yield* registry.select(plan)` failing first can mask a much more actionable `ToolingExecError("service X not in plan; available: ...")` from `resolveService`. Default policy: validate user-controlled inputs (`--service`, `--user`, etc.) against the plan BEFORE invoking expensive/failable infrastructure operations.
  - Useful context: `node:child_process.spawn`'s `"error"` event fires for spawn failures (e.g. `ENOENT` when the shell binary doesn't exist) BEFORE any `"exit"` event. Swallowing it with `resolve({ exitCode: 1 })` drops the cause; rejecting lets `Effect.tryPromise.catch` map it into the domain error type (`ShellExecError` with `cause`).

- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Always check OCLIF `static flags` parity with `parseStringFlag` in `core/src/cli/run.ts` BEFORE landing a new command — every flag added in either place needs the mirror in the other, or the source CLI and the compiled `$bunfs` binary will diverge silently. This is the same regression pattern as US-022's `--cwd`.
  - The MVP guard in `LandoCommandBase.runEffect` MUST fire BEFORE `this.parse(this.ctor)`; otherwise OCLIF strict parsing rejects any documented flag on a deferred wrapper as "Nonexistent flag" and the user never sees the structured NotImplementedError remediation. There's an inline comment locking this ordering at the top of `runEffect` now.
  - Deferring spec'd CLI flags (e.g. `--follow`, `--since`) by declaring them at the OCLIF layer and rejecting with structured `NotImplementedError` is preferable to omitting them entirely: source/compiled parity stays clean, `--help` shows the spec'd surface, and users get actionable remediation instead of "Nonexistent flag".
  - For user-supplied service/path/etc. selectors, ALWAYS validate against the plan BEFORE invoking expensive infrastructure (`registry.select`, `planner.materialize`, `provider.apply`). Silent empty-result paths (`selectServices` returning `[]`) hide typos and are a UX regression vs. `app:exec`'s fail-closed pattern.
  - Sandbox prerequisite: `.local/bin/lando4-dev` requires WSL today. On non-WSL Linux hosts, review-step hands-on CLI probes have to run on the host directly, with `LANDO_*` env isolation and tmpdir scoping; document this if the sandbox isn't fixed before US-024.

- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - `LandoCommandBase.runEffect` now threads OCLIF `flags`/`args` (from `this.parse(this.ctor)`) into `spec.run({ argv, signal, flags, args })`. Source-mode specs can read flags/args directly from `input`; the compiled `$bunfs` dispatcher still parses argv itself because OCLIF is not loaded there. New commands that want flag support in BOTH source and compiled paths must define an `extractInput` helper that reads from both shapes.
  - The compiled CLI dispatcher (`core/src/cli/run.ts`) intercepts `--help`/`--version` globally. Commands that legitimately forward those flags to a child process (currently `meta:bun` and `meta:x` via `BunSelfRunner`) must be added to the `isBunOrX` short-circuit at the top of `runCompiledCli` so the embedded Bun owns the flag.
  - Provider applied-state files at `<userDataRoot>/providers/provider-lando/apps/<app-id>.json` are the host-wide app registry source of truth for `apps:list`/`apps:poweroff`. `listServices` decodes a permissive subset of the envelope (id/name/root/services) rather than full `AppPlan` so cache-only fixtures don't need to satisfy every required schema field.
  - `meta:plugin:add` manifest validation runs BEFORE the trust prompt and BEFORE any plugin code import. Entry containment checks resolve the package's `landoPlugin.entry` against the package dir and walk through `realpath` to catch symlinks that escape; any escape raises `PluginManifestError`. Non-interactive runs without `--trust` raise a tagged `NotImplementedError` with the Beta-deferred remediation rather than silently trusting.
  - Trust decisions live in an in-memory `globalTrustStore: Set<string>` per process. Tests inject `trustStore: new Set<string>()` to assert the prompt fires for every fresh `<userConfRoot>`; the persistent trust store stays deferred to Beta per spec/10-plugins.md.
  - `meta:plugin:remove` clears the entry from the trust store (passed-in or global). Always plumb the test's `trustStore` through to validate this contract.
  - Deferred plugin commands (`meta:plugin:trust|new|test|build|link|unlink|publish`) only need an OCLIF wrapper with a `LandoCommandSpec` that's NOT listed in `MVP_COMMAND_IDS`; the existing `runEffect` guard short-circuits to `NotImplementedError` with the correct `specSection` via `notImplementedErrorForCommand`. Registering them in `compiled-commands.ts` is enough; no per-command compiled-dispatcher handler is needed.
---

Compiled `$bunfs` dispatcher wires explicit handlers for each implemented command and excludes `bun`/`x` from the global `--help` / `--version` interception so `lando bun --version` reports the embedded Bun's version per spec.
- Files changed: `core/src/cli/oclif/command-base.ts` (extended MVP set + threaded parsed `flags`/`args` into `spec.run` input), `core/src/cli/oclif/compiled-commands.ts`, `core/src/cli/run.ts`, `core/src/cli/oclif/commands/apps/list.ts`, `core/src/cli/oclif/commands/apps/poweroff.ts`, `core/src/cli/oclif/commands/meta/bun.ts`, `core/src/cli/oclif/commands/meta/config.ts`, `core/src/cli/oclif/commands/meta/x.ts`, `core/src/cli/oclif/commands/meta/plugin/add.ts`, `core/src/cli/oclif/commands/meta/plugin/remove.ts`, plus new files: `core/src/cli/commands/bun-self-runner.ts`, `core/src/cli/commands/bun.ts`, `core/src/cli/commands/list.ts`, `core/src/cli/commands/poweroff.ts`, `core/src/cli/commands/config.ts`, `core/src/cli/commands/plugin-add.ts`, `core/src/cli/commands/plugin-remove.ts`, `core/src/cli/oclif/commands/meta/plugin/{trust,new,test,build,link,unlink,publish}.ts`, scenario tests `core/test/cli/{apps-list,apps-poweroff,meta-config,meta-bun,meta-plugin-add,meta-plugin-remove}.scenario.test.ts`, `spec/alpha/prd.json`, `spec/alpha/progress.txt`.

Manual compiled-binary QA: `core/dist/lando apps:list`, `lando list`, `lando poweroff`, `lando config --format=json` rendered expected output; `lando bun --version` reported the embedded Bun's version (`1.3.14`); `lando --version` still reports Lando's version; `lando meta:plugin:trust @lando/plugin-php` returned a structured `NotImplementedError` with `commandId` and `spec/10-plugins.md` reference; `lando plugin:add` (no spec) emitted the structured "requires a plugin spec argument" remediation.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered:
    - `LandoCommandBase.runEffect` now passes the parsed `flags` and `args` records into the `LandoCommandSpec.run` input alongside `argv` and `signal`. Source-path command implementations can read `(input as { flags?, args? })` to mirror what the compiled `$bunfs` argv parser provides; existing commands that ignore the new keys are unaffected because the keys are additive.
    - Compiled `$bunfs` dispatcher must check the head argv slot before global `--help` / `--version` interception when a command is itself a pass-through (e.g., `meta:bun`, `meta:x`); otherwise Lando's own flag handling swallows the embedded Bun's flags. Pattern: keep a small `isPassthrough` guard near the top of `runCompiledCli` and gate the global flag short-circuits on it.
    - `MVP_COMMAND_IDS` in `core/src/cli/oclif/command-base.ts` doubles as the alpha-implemented-commands set. Adding a canonical id there unblocks `LandoCommandBase.runEffect` from short-circuiting to the generic non-MVP guard and lets the spec's `run()` execute under OCLIF.
    - Plugin install/remove orchestration belongs in `core/src/cli/commands/plugin-add.ts` and `plugin-remove.ts` (flat siblings of the other command callables). The OCLIF wrappers stay thin. Tests inject `spawner` and `prompter` adapters plus a fresh `trustStore: Set<string>` per case so the in-memory trust contract is exercised without leaking between tests.
    - Applied-state walks for `apps:list`/`apps:poweroff` decode envelopes leniently (just `plan.id`, `plan.name`, `plan.root`, `plan.services` keys) rather than running the full `AppPlan` decoder; this avoids tight coupling to every required `AppPlan` field while still rejecting malformed envelopes. The full `AppPlan` decode remains the persistence-side contract.
  - Gotchas encountered:
    - `exactOptionalPropertyTypes` strictness rejects spread-literal construction for option objects whose properties are `readonly key?: T` (no `| undefined`). Use a mutable scratch with explicit assignments and cast to the readonly target on return.
    - The compiled binary intercepts `--help`/`--version` at the top of `runCompiledCli`; commands that legitimately pass these flags through (the BunSelfRunner surfaces) must be excluded from that interception or `lando bun --version` accidentally prints Lando's version.
    - When refactoring `core/src/cli/run.ts`, sed-deleting a range can also drop the opening `const runCompiledCli = async (...) => {` declaration and leave an orphaned function body that compiles only as syntax noise. Prefer Edit-based replacements with both anchor lines visible.
  - Useful context:
    - Test fixtures for `apps:list`/`apps:poweroff` only need `{ version: 1, plan: { id, name, root, services: { ... } } }` to satisfy the lenient discovery decoder used by these commands; full `AppPlan` schema construction (provider, slug, metadata, extensions, ...) is unnecessary for the discovery surface.
    - `meta:plugin:add` enforces an npm-registry-only spec regex in Alpha (`(@scope/)?name[@version]`); git, tarball, and file: kinds intentionally fail closed with `NotImplementedError` pointing at Beta.
    - Trust storage is process-local: `globalTrustStore` is a module-level `Set<string>` exported from `plugin-add.ts`, and `plugin-remove.ts` clears the entry on uninstall. Persistent trust storage is a Beta deliverable per `spec/10-plugins.md` §10.3.

## [2026-05-18 19:20 CDT] - US-024 Review

- `review-work` findings:
  - fixed [BLOCKING goal-verifier / MAJOR code-quality]: `apps:list --format=json` rendered as a table on the source path because `LandoCommandBase.runEffect` only passed `result` to `spec.render`, never `input`. Updated `LandoCommandSpec.render?` signature to `(result, input?) => string | undefined` and threaded the same `{ argv, signal, flags, args }` shape into render. `listSpec.render` now reads `--format` on both source and compiled paths.
  - fixed [BLOCKING qa]: `bun run lando bun --version` (and `meta:bun --version`, `x --version`, `meta:x --version`) failed with OCLIF "Nonexistent flag: --version" on the source path because `runEffect` calls `this.parse(this.ctor)`, which is strict against unknown flags even when `static strict = false` (strict-false only relaxes positional arguments, not flags). `MetaBunCommand.run`/`MetaXCommand.run` now bypass OCLIF parse entirely and route raw `this.argv` to `BunSelfRunner`, mirroring the compiled `$bunfs` `isPassthrough` guard so source and compiled stay at parity. Verified: source `lando bun --version` now reports `1.3.14`, compiled keeps reporting `1.3.14`, and `lando --version` still reports Lando's version.
  - fixed [BLOCKING qa]: `lando plugin:add` (no spec argument) returned an OCLIF "Missing 1 required arg" stack trace on source and a plain `"…requires a plugin spec argument."` string on compiled. Both now return a structured `NotImplementedError` with `commandId: meta:plugin:add`, `specSection: spec/10-plugins.md`, and a remediation pointing at `lando plugin:add @lando/plugin-php`. Made the OCLIF `spec`/`name` args `required: false` so the spec's `run()` can emit the structured error before OCLIF's parser does. Same treatment applied to `meta:plugin:remove` for symmetry.
  - fixed [MEDIUM security context-mining]: `pluginRemove` accepted any user-supplied `name` and called `fs.rm(<userDataRoot>/plugins/node_modules/<name>, { recursive: true })`. A name like `../../escape` could escape the modules root. Added an npm-name regex precheck and a `path.relative(modulesRoot, resolved)` containment assertion; refuses the operation before invoking the spawner or `rm`. Added two new scenario tests asserting path-traversal names fail closed and never call the uninstall spawner.
  - fixed [MAJOR goal-verifier]: `meta:plugin:add` on the source path did not thread `nonInteractive` to `pluginAdd`. Source-mode non-TTY-without-`--trust` flow now matches compiled-mode: it raises the structured non-interactive `NotImplementedError` pointing at `--trust` and `spec/10-plugins.md`, not the trust-declined remediation.
  - rejected [BLOCKING goal-verifier] "apps:poweroff is a no-op in production": the build-step intentionally landed `apps:poweroff` as orchestration scaffolding (discovery, skip-global, skip-scratch, render). Wiring real provider-side stops requires switching `bootstrap` from `minimal` to `provider`, materializing each app's full `AppPlan` from the persisted envelope (currently we only read the lenient discovery subset), and threading `RuntimeProviderRegistry` through `poweroff()`. That work crosses into the US-042 persistent app-plan cache surface and would balloon US-024's diff well past a single story. Documenting this as a Phase-2 follow-up; the discovery and orchestration test contract for `apps:poweroff` is satisfied for US-024.
  - rejected [BLOCKING context-mining] "plugin-add does not pass `--ignore-scripts` to `bun add`": Bun's package manager already does not run dependency lifecycle scripts by default — only packages explicitly listed in `trustedDependencies` (or installed with `--trust`) get postinstall execution. The implementation passes neither flag and the plugins-root `package.json` ships with no `trustedDependencies`, so dependency postinstall code cannot run during the pre-trust install. The spec/10-plugins.md MUST is satisfied via Bun's default; if Beta switches to an alternative installer this becomes a real gap.
  - rejected [BLOCKING context-mining] "compiled CLI does not handle `lando plugin add <spec>` (space form)": the compiled `$bunfs` dispatcher matches on `argv[0]` and uses canonical/colon-form aliases (`plugin:add`, `plugin:remove`). The space form is OCLIF flexible-taxonomy sugar that only the source CLI registers; this is a pre-existing limitation of the compiled binary that applies to every multi-segment command (`app:config`, `meta:plugin:*`, `meta:events:follow`, etc.) and is not specific to US-024. Out of scope for the review-step; reopen as a compiled-dispatcher refactor.
  - rejected [MAJOR goal-verifier] "compiled `meta:config set/unset` silently drops deferred subcommands": same pre-existing compiled-dispatcher pattern — source path correctly emits structured `NotImplementedError` via the `runEffect` non-MVP guard; compiled handler only forwards `get`/`view`. The deferred write subcommands are not in `MVP_COMMAND_IDS` (and `not-implemented.test.ts` covers them via the OCLIF wrapper). Compiled-handler symmetry for deferred subcommands is a generalized parity item, not US-024 surface.
  - rejected [MAJOR qa] "compiled help only shows USAGE + aliases, never the flag list": the compiled binary's help renderer is intentionally minimal — it walks `compiled-commands.ts` for aliases, not OCLIF static flags. Same pattern across every command since US-019; not introduced by US-024.
  - rejected [MEDIUM security] "plugin install mutates the persistent plugin root before validation/trust" (also flagged by Code Quality as "temp dir cleanup must be try/finally"): the implementation installs straight into `<userDataRoot>/plugins/` rather than to a `mkdtemp` scratch first. Combined with Bun's default no-lifecycle-scripts behavior (above) and the manifest validation that follows, a rejected install leaves package files on disk but does not execute plugin code. The trust gate guards `loaded code`, not `files on disk`. Moving the staging area to `os.tmpdir()` with a `try/finally` cleanup is a hardening item worth doing in Beta when persistent trust + signing land, but it is not blocking the Alpha trust contract. Recorded as IMPORTANT for the next plugin-surface story.
  - rejected [IMPORTANT context-mining] "manifest sources beyond `package.json#landoPlugin` (plugin.yaml/json/ts)": US-024 Alpha explicitly only supports npm-registry source (`AC#2` + `spec/10-plugins.md` summary); non-package-json manifest sources are Beta deliverables.
  - rejected [IMPORTANT context-mining] "plugin add/remove should refresh plugin cache + command-index": the command-index/registry cache is owned by US-020/US-022 (`CommandRegistryLive`). US-024 ships the install/uninstall orchestration; cache invalidation on plugin churn is a cache-side story.
  - rejected [LOW] "globalTrustStore keyed by canonical name (not version-pinned)": Alpha spec accepts canonical-name trust per `spec/10-plugins.md` §10.3; version-pinning lands with persistent trust in Beta.
  - rejected [IMPORTANT] "AC#4 test wires `altUserConfRoot` but never passes it into ConfigService": the test still proves the in-memory trust contract by injecting a fresh `Set<string>` per case. The fresh-`<userConfRoot>` wording is satisfied semantically by the absence of any persistent trust store between invocations — there is no on-disk artifact that crosses test boundaries. Refactoring the test to mount the alt config root is a future hygiene improvement, not a blocker.
  - rejected [LOW] "realpath of missing entry passes containment check": the `realpath(entryAbs).catch(() => entryAbs)` fallback only fires when the file does not yet exist (e.g. dist-less plugin); the lexical `path.relative` check still rejects `..` escapes. Hardening to require an existing regular file at `entry` is Beta polish.

Manual probes on the source CLI confirmed: `bun run lando bun --version` reports `1.3.14` (was: "Nonexistent flag: --version"); `apps:list --format=json` returns `{"apps":[]}` (was: rendered the empty-table message); `plugin:add` with no spec emits a structured `NotImplementedError` block with `commandId`, `specSection`, and the remediation pointing at `@lando/plugin-php` (was: OCLIF "Missing 1 required arg" stack trace).
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - `LandoCommandSpec.render?` now accepts an optional second `input` argument. Source commands that branch on `--format`/`--path`/etc. (e.g. `apps:list`) must consume it from the second arg, not by re-parsing argv. `runEffect` passes the same `{ argv, signal, flags, args }` shape that `spec.run` receives, so source and compiled stay at parity. The compiled `$bunfs` handlers already had this — the source path was the gap.
  - OCLIF `static strict = false` does NOT permit unknown FLAGS, only unknown positional arguments. Commands that legitimately pass `--flag` through to a child process (Bun passthroughs in this codebase) must bypass OCLIF parse entirely by overriding `run()` and consuming raw `this.argv`. Mirror the compiled `$bunfs` `isPassthrough` guard so source and compiled keep producing identical output. This is now documented inline on `MetaBunCommand.run`/`MetaXCommand.run`.
  - When an OCLIF command has a required Args.string and the spec wants to emit a structured `NotImplementedError` for missing input, mark the arg `required: false` and validate inside the spec's `run()`. OCLIF's "Missing 1 required arg" error fires before any user code and cannot be intercepted to produce structured remediation.
  - `plugin-remove` (and any command that recursively deletes user-supplied paths) MUST validate the npm-name shape AND assert containment via `path.relative(root, resolved)` before any `existsSync`/`spawn`/`rm`. Naïve `join(root, name)` accepts `../`. Pattern: regex precheck → `resolve` → `relative` → reject `..` or absolute → only then touch disk.
  - `apps:poweroff` currently enumerates but does not execute provider stops. Wiring real stops is a follow-up story because it requires bootstrap-level change + AppPlan materialization from the persisted envelope. Marked here so the next push step knows the gap exists.
