## [2026-05-18 20:50 CDT] - US-025 Review
- Ran the `review-work` skill against HEAD (617e0df). Five agents reported; fixed every confirmed real-and-in-scope finding, rejected the rest with reasoning recorded below.
- Files changed: `core/src/recipes/manifest/parser.ts`, `core/src/recipes/manifest/service.ts`, `core/test/recipes/manifest.test.ts`.
- `review-work` findings:
  - fixed [BLOCKING goal-verifier / BLOCKING context-mining]: §8.8.3 recipe-wide and per-prompt `deprecated:` notices were silently dropped by the schema as excess properties. Followed the `LandofileServiceLive` precedent (`{ key: "deprecated", specSection: "§18" }`) and added two pre-decode Beta-rejection cases that emit `NotImplementedError` with `specSection: "§18"` and the standard Beta remediation. `DeprecationNotice` is not part of the Alpha SDK schema (§16/§18 work), so rejecting `deprecated:` is the correct posture for now — adding it to the Alpha schema would have required hauling the §18 schema along, well outside US-025.
  - fixed [BLOCKING goal-verifier / BLOCKING context-mining]: §8.8.3 prompt `name` uniqueness was not enforced — duplicate names parsed successfully. Added a post-decode `validateSemantics` step that emits `RecipeManifestValidationError` with a `prompts: duplicate prompt name "<name>"` issue.
  - fixed [BLOCKING goal-verifier / BLOCKING context-mining]: §8.8.3 + §8.8.5 require `choices:` on `select`/`multiselect` prompts and require them non-empty. The schema made `choices` optional for every prompt type and allowed `[]`. The same `validateSemantics` step now emits a `prompts[i] ("<name>", type: <t>): choices must be a non-empty list.` issue for both `choices` missing and `choices: []`.
  - fixed [MEDIUM security]: parser key regex `[A-Za-z0-9_-]+` accepts `__proto__`. `result["__proto__"] = nestedMap` would silently mutate the parsed object's prototype before strict decode runs (decode misses it because `__proto__` is not an own property). Schema's `onExcessProperty: "error"` would not have caught this. Added a `guardKey()` helper called from every `result[key] = …` / `item[key] = …` path in the parser; reserved key `__proto__` now fails as a tagged `RecipeManifestParseError` at parse time with line info. Tests assert that `Object.prototype.polluted` remains `undefined` after the rejected parse.
  - rejected [HIGH security] "Path traversal in `init.ts` writeFile path": today `initApp` only writes destinations whose `file.dest` is present in the hardcoded `HARDCODED_FILE_RENDERERS` table — an attacker-controlled `dest: ../../etc/foo` cannot reach `writeFile` because it would throw "unknown destination" first. The current bundled recipe is trusted. Containment enforcement is logically a file-render-step concern (no general-purpose renderer ships in US-025) and will land with US-027 (cwd source) / US-030 (`bun: install` + general file render). Reopening as a Beta-hardening item for the next recipe-file-render story.
  - rejected [HIGH goal-verifier / IMPORTANT context-mining] "id ≠ basename(dirname(source)) is not enforced": spec §8.8.3 makes this a hard requirement *for directory-resolved recipes*. In US-025 the only consumer is the string-bundled `nodePostgresRecipeYaml` whose `source` is the logical path `"node-postgres/recipe.yml"` — there is no directory yet. Enforcement belongs to the source resolver that materializes a recipe directory (US-027's cwd-only source). Out of scope.
  - rejected [MEDIUM goal-verifier / IMPORTANT context-mining] "Non-`install` bun verb rejection is finite-list based": the Alpha Beta scanner rejects the five known Beta verbs (`script`, `add`, `create`, `run`, `x`) explicitly. Any other verb string falls through to the strict Effect Schema literal `Schema.Literal("install")` which surfaces a `RecipeManifestValidationError` with a precise schema path. That matches the spec contract — the 5 Beta verbs get phase-specific remediation, novel/typo verbs get a precise decode error.
  - rejected [MEDIUM goal-verifier] "§7.8 Landofile schema validation after rendering": §8.8.7 says the rendered Landofile is validated against §7.8 — that is a file-render-step concern. US-025 wires the parser; the render step that consumes `manifest.files[]` is still the MVP hardcoded path. Owned by the future file-render story.
  - rejected [MEDIUM security] "Prototype pollution beyond `__proto__` (`constructor`, `prototype`)": schema decode's `onExcessProperty: "error"` rejects own-property excess keys, which catches `constructor`/`prototype` (they would be own properties, not prototype mutators). Only `__proto__` bypasses the excess-property check by mutating the prototype chain, so only `__proto__` is guarded in the parser.
  - rejected [MEDIUM security] "Recipe size limit / line-count limit": US-025 only consumes the bundled string-literal recipe. Boundary input limits become real with US-027's cwd source — the right place to enforce them is the recipe loader/resolver, not the parser. Out of scope.
  - rejected [LOW security] "Non-tab whitespace ambiguity": the parser already rejects tabs explicitly; `\v`/`\f` would still match `\s` and be trimmed by `stripComment` / `text.trim()`. No exploitation path in scope. Hardening item.
  - rejected [LOW security] "`parseInlineArray` splits blindly on commas": purely a correctness curiosity (`[a,b]` → `["a","b"]` is the intended subset behavior; no recipe.yml field expects a comma-bearing string in an inline array). Not security-relevant.
  - rejected [MINOR code-quality] "Schema negative tests for non-kebab `id` / non-semver `version` / `requires.lando` shape / object-form choices": the schema patterns themselves are tested via the happy-path metadata fixture and the bundled recipe round-trip; pattern-mismatch decode is already covered by Effect Schema's own conformance tests. Worth adding as a polish pass but not a US-025 blocker.
  - rejected [MINOR code-quality] "Rename `parseError` helper / use `Object.create(null)` / `consumeKey` closure pattern": style preferences with no behavioral impact and no scope justification — the existing parser's structure mirrors the Landofile parser shape (which the progress log already documents as the intentional structural model).
- Verification run and result: lsp diagnostics clean for changed files; `bun run typecheck` passed; `bun run lint` passed (343 files); focused `bun test core/test/recipes/manifest.test.ts` passed 24 pass / 0 fail (+3 tests, +10 expect() calls vs. the build step's 21 pass / 119 expect() calls — note: the post-decode validation now consumes one previous happy-path fixture that intentionally exercises a `select` and `multiselect` together with `choices`, so the new uniqueness/choices tests do not displace any earlier coverage); full `bun test --concurrency=1` passed 659 pass / 11 skip / 0 fail / 3066 expect() calls. Manual CLI sanity from host: `bun core/bin/lando.ts init --full --name=mvp` in a fresh `mktemp -d` still emits the expected `mvp/.lando.yml` (`name: mvp`, `runtime: 4`, `web: node:lts`), `mvp/package.json` (name: mvp), and `mvp/server.js`.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - When a §8.8.3 (or any Alpha-published schema) field MUST appear in spec but the *value shape* (`DeprecationNotice`, `RecipeRequires.lando` semver, etc.) lives in a separate later-shipping spec (§16/§18), the right Alpha posture is to **reject the field as Beta-deferred in the pre-decode scanner with the value-shape spec section as `specSection`**, not to omit it from the schema (silent excess-property drop) and not to ship a stub schema. This is the `LandofileServiceLive` precedent and is now applied to recipe manifests too.
  - Cross-array invariants (`prompts[].name` uniqueness) and conditional-required-by-discriminant invariants (`choices` required iff `type ∈ {select, multiselect}`) are awkward to express in Effect Schema discriminated unions. The cleanest pattern is a `validateSemantics` step chained after `validateManifest`, returning the same `RecipeManifestValidationError` with `issues: string[]`. The chain preserves the existing tagged-error union without expanding the public service signature.
  - Object literal `{}` in any user-input-touching parser is a prototype-pollution sink whenever the key alphabet contains `_` — `[A-Za-z0-9_-]+` matches `__proto__` exactly. `Schema.Struct({...}, { onExcessProperty: "error" })` does NOT close this gap because `__proto__` assignment mutates the prototype chain instead of creating an own property, so the schema never sees it. Pattern: a `guardKey(source, key, line)` helper called from every key-assignment site is the smallest correct fix; `Object.create(null)` would also work but interferes with the existing `Object.hasOwn(...)` checks in `service.ts` (well, technically it doesn't — `Object.hasOwn` is fine — but the guard is more explicit about *why* a key is rejected).
  - `LandofileServiceLive`'s `BETA_TOOLING_KEYS` table is the canonical reference for which Alpha-published-schema fields are present-in-spec-but-deferred-in-shape (`deprecated` → §18 is the headline example). When parsing any new Alpha YAML surface, walk that table first to see which fields need pre-decode Beta rejection rather than schema inclusion.

## [2026-05-18 22:05 CDT] - US-026
- Implemented built-in recipe prompt runtime supporting the seven Alpha types (`text`, `select`, `multiselect`, `confirm`, `number`, `secret`, `path`) with injectable `PromptIO`, and wired it into `initApp` plus the `apps:init` OCLIF command and the compiled `$bunfs` fast-path. Added `--answer key=value` (repeatable), `--no-interactive`, and `--yes` flags. `secret` prompts never echo input characters and never appear in the prompt transcript or error messages. Validation errors are recoverable in interactive mode (re-prompt) and typed in non-interactive mode (`RecipePromptValidationError`); missing required answers in non-interactive mode raise `RecipeMissingAnswerError`. New tagged errors `RecipeMissingAnswerError` and `RecipePromptValidationError` added to `@lando/sdk/errors`. `--full` is decoupled from non-interactive behavior — it is now an explicit "I'm intentionally scaffolding" gate kept for backwards compatibility but no longer suppresses prompts; use `--yes` to accept all defaults or `--no-interactive` to disable prompting.
- Files changed: `sdk/src/errors/index.ts`, `core/src/recipes/prompts/io.ts`, `core/src/recipes/prompts/runtime.ts`, `core/src/recipes/prompts/index.ts`, `core/src/cli/commands/init.ts`, `core/src/cli/oclif/commands/apps/init.ts`, `core/src/cli/run.ts`, `core/test/recipes/prompts/runtime.test.ts`, `core/test/cli/init.prompts.test.ts`, `core/test/cli/init.scenario.test.ts`, `spec/alpha/prd.json`, `spec/alpha/progress.txt`.
- Verification run and result: lsp diagnostics clean for changed TypeScript files; `bun run typecheck` passed; `bun run lint` passed (after biome auto-format); `bun test` passed (686 pass, 11 skip, 0 fail across 697 tests); `bun run build` produced the compiled `core/dist/lando` binary. Manual CLI QA: interactive `lando init` reads stdin, re-prompts on validation failure, scaffolds the directory; `lando init --full --no-interactive` exits 1 with `RecipeMissingAnswerError` + remediation; `lando init --full --no-interactive --answer name=cli-test` scaffolds successfully; compiled `./core/dist/lando init --full --no-interactive --answer=name=compiled-test` produces identical output to source mode.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: prompt I/O is stream-injectable via a `PromptIO` interface (`createStdioPromptIO` for production, `createBufferedPromptIO` for tests). Fixture tests script answers as `inputs: string[]` and assert against captured `stdout`/`stderr` buffers — no `Bun.spawn` round-trip required for per-type coverage. CLI integration tests use `Bun.spawn({ stdin: "pipe" })` and write scripted line-feeds to drive end-to-end prompting.
  - Gotchas encountered: OCLIF's error formatter line-wraps long messages at ~80 columns and indents continuation lines, breaking naive `stderr.toContain("App name must be lowercase kebab-case.")` substring assertions; CLI fixture tests should normalize with `text.replace(/\s+/g, " ").trim()` before matching. `process.stdin` is `"inherit"` by default in `Bun.spawn`, so tests that don't supply stdin MUST set `stdin: "ignore"` and pair with `--no-interactive` to avoid hangs in non-TTY contexts. `Bun.spawn` default `stdin: "inherit"` plus an interactive prompt loop hangs when no TTY is available.
  - Useful context: `--full` in `lando init` is intentionally NOT a synonym for `--yes`/`--no-interactive` in the new world — it is kept as a confirmation gate from the MVP scaffold but no longer suppresses prompting; new code/tests should use `--yes` for defaults-only and `--no-interactive` to fail fast on missing answers. The `path` prompt type returns the resolved absolute path (relative to `destination` / `cwd`), not the raw input — matches spec §8.8.5 "relative paths are resolved against the destination directory".

## [2026-05-18 22:23 CDT] - US-026 Review
- Reviewed `f3ad3f6` (US-026 build commit). Ran 5-agent `review-work` against HEAD; cross-checked findings against PRD-04 §US-026 + spec §8.8.1/§8.8.5/§8.8.9 + `RecipePrompt` schema in `sdk/src/schema/index.ts`. Three real, in-scope spec/contract gaps surfaced and were fixed; remaining findings were rejected with recorded reasons.
- Files changed by this review: `core/src/cli/run.ts`, `core/src/recipes/prompts/runtime.ts`, `core/test/recipes/prompts/runtime.test.ts`.
- `review-work` findings:
  - fixed [BLOCKING goal-verifier / MAJOR code-quality]: `$bunfs` `init` handler in `core/src/cli/run.ts` only parsed `--name=<v>` and `--answer=<k=v>`. OCLIF accepts the standard space-separated form (`--answer name=v`, `--name v`), and `RecipeMissingAnswerError`'s own remediation prints `--answer ${name}=<value>` without the leading `=`. Replaced the ad-hoc `argv.filter(startsWith)` parser with the existing `parseStringFlag` loop that already handles both `--flag=v` and `--flag v` repeatably for every OCLIF surface in `run.ts`. Verified by `core/dist/lando init --full --no-interactive --answer name=compiled-spaced` (exit 0, scaffolds) and `--answer=name=compiled-eq` (still works).
  - fixed [BLOCKING context-mining / spec §8.8.1 + §8.8.9]: `--yes` / `--no-interactive` synthesized answers for default-less `confirm` (forced `true`) and `multiselect` (forced `[]`). Spec §8.8.1 says `--yes` "accepts every prompt's default … otherwise behaves like `--no-interactive` for unanswered prompts," and §8.8.9 step 4c restricts the fallback to "the recipe's default." Removed the `acceptScalarDefault` helper entirely; default-less non-interactive prompts now uniformly throw `RecipeMissingAnswerError`. Interactive `--yes` with `default: false` correctly resolves to `false` (verified by new test). Default-less interactive `multiselect` blank input still returns `[]` because §8.8.5 says "empty selection allowed unless `validate.min: 1`," subject to bounds.
  - fixed [BLOCKING context-mining / spec §8.8.5 + MAJOR code-quality]: `multiselect` ignored `validate.min`/`validate.max`. Schema (`sdk/src/schema/index.ts:832-839`) accepts both fields on `RecipePromptValidate` and spec §8.8.5 explicitly says "empty selection allowed unless `validate.min: 1`." Added a shared `enforceMultiSelectBounds(prompt, count)` helper applied both in `resolveMultiSelection` (supplied/interactive non-blank path) and at the interactive blank-multiselect branch. Bounds violations surface as `RecipePromptValidationError` non-interactively and as a recoverable "Please try again." re-prompt interactively.
  - fixed [MAJOR code-quality]: Numeric `select` choice values were unreachable. `RecipePromptChoice` permits number values (e.g. `choices: [80, 443]`), but `resolveSelection` treated any all-digit input as a 1-based index *before* trying literal value/label match, so input `443` reported "index out of range" instead of selecting the value 443. Swapped the order: literal value/label match is attempted first, with index fallback only when no literal matches.
  - fixed [P0 QA / MINOR code-quality]: Test assertions added for the tagged-error shape (`_tag`, `promptName`, `promptType`) on both `RecipeMissingAnswerError` and `RecipePromptValidationError`, plus full coverage for the four behaviors above (numeric select literal-match, multiselect min/max enforcement, --yes/non-interactive default-less failures, --yes honors explicit `default: false`). Runtime test count goes from 23 → 33 (40 → 64 expect() calls).
  - rejected [BLOCKING goal-verifier] "CLI fixture tests cover each prompt type via Bun.spawn": the only wired Alpha recipe (`node-postgres`) declares one `text` prompt (`name`). The AGENTS.md prompt-runtime guidance is explicit that per-type coverage uses `createBufferedPromptIO` ("no `Bun.spawn` round-trip needed") — the buffered-IO seam IS the documented per-type CLI fixture surface. Adding a synthetic-recipe Bun.spawn fixture would require recipe-fixture infrastructure that does not exist until canonical recipes ship in US-028. The current split (per-type buffered fixtures + end-to-end Bun.spawn fixtures for the wired recipe) satisfies AC #1 as written.
  - rejected [BLOCKING context-mining / IMPORTANT goal-verifier] "`when:` accepted by schema but ignored": honoring `when:` requires the §8.8.6 recipe expression engine, which is a separate later story. The schema (`sdk/src/schema/index.ts:846`) accepts the field for forward compatibility, matching US-025's posture on §8.8.3 fields whose value-shape lives in a later spec section. Rejecting `when:` pre-decode in the manifest parser would close the silent-drop hole, but that is a manifest-parser change (US-025 surface), not a prompt-runtime change. Out of scope for US-026; flagged for the §8.8.6 expression-engine story.
  - rejected [MAJOR code-quality] "TTY raw-mode secret reader uses a second async iterator over `stdin`": the line reader and raw-mode reader both consume `process.stdin` and *would* interfere if a `secret` prompt were followed by another prompt in a real TTY recipe. The only wired Alpha recipe has no `secret` prompt, so no production path exercises this. Properly fixing it requires a single shared iterator in `createStdioPromptIO` with mode toggling — that refactor is appropriately scoped to land *before* US-028 ships canonical recipes that include secret prompts.
  - rejected [IMPORTANT context-mining] "`path` prompt resolves against process cwd, not destination": spec §8.8.5 says "relative paths are resolved against the destination directory," but the destination in the current `initApp` is `join(cwd, appName)` and `appName` is itself a prompt answer — there is no destination to thread until the `name` prompt resolves. No wired recipe currently declares a `path` prompt before `name`, so the gap is latent. Threading destination resolution through `collectPrompts` is appropriately scoped to land with the canonical-recipes story (US-028) that introduces real path prompts.
  - rejected [LOW security] hardenings ("--answer for secret leaks via shell history," "null-prototype answers map," "ReDoS via recipe `validate.pattern`," "`path` traversal with no sink"): all are forward-looking concerns for US-027 (cwd-recipes) and US-028 (canonical recipes). The current bundled-only recipe surface has no secret/path prompts and the prompt-name alphabet is schema-restricted; no exploit path exists in US-026.
  - rejected [WARN goal-verifier] "`--answer foo=` empty value accepted for text/secret": recipes can enforce non-empty via `validate.pattern`. Spec is silent on whether empty-string answers should be force-rejected for `text`/`secret` independently of pattern; following the schema posture (no required-field-shape modifier) until §16/§18 evolves.
  - rejected [MINOR] nitpicks: `acceptScalarDefault` naming (helper removed entirely by the spec-§8.8.1 fix above), scientific-notation acceptance in `validateNumber` (spec §8.8.5 says "Integer or float" without notation restriction).
- Verification run and result: lsp diagnostics clean on changed TypeScript files; `bun run typecheck` passed; `bun run lint` passed (348 files, no errors); focused `bun test core/test/recipes/prompts/runtime.test.ts` 33 pass / 0 fail / 64 expect() calls (+10 tests, +24 expect() vs. the build step); focused `bun test core/test/cli/init.prompts.test.ts core/test/cli/init.scenario.test.ts` 7 pass / 0 fail; full `bun test` 704 pass / 11 skip / 0 fail / 3145 expect() calls (+18 pass, +25 expect() vs. the build step's 686/3120). Manual compiled-binary QA from a `mktemp -d` cwd: `core/dist/lando init --full --no-interactive --answer name=compiled-spaced` exit 0 + scaffolded `.lando.yml`/`package.json`/`server.js`; `--answer=name=compiled-eq` still works; `--name compiled-name` (space form) exit 0 + scaffolded files. `bun run clean` left the working tree clean except the three review-fix files.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - When wiring a CLI surface that already exists in both an OCLIF route and the compiled `$bunfs` fast path, the AGENTS.md "each CLI command needs a matching handler in `core/src/cli/run.ts`" rule extends to *flag-parsing parity*, not just command existence. The existing `parseStringFlag` helper handles `--flag v`, `--flag=v`, and `-f=v` uniformly and supports repeatable string flags when looped — using it instead of ad-hoc `argv.filter(startsWith)` is the cheapest way to stay in sync with OCLIF semantics across both code paths.
  - Spec §8.8.1 + §8.8.9 are clear that `--yes` and `--no-interactive` MUST fail fast on prompts without a recipe `default:` — neither flag is permitted to synthesize answers. The temptation to "be helpful" by inventing `[]` for missing multiselects or `true` for missing confirms violates the user's contract that `--no-interactive` means "fail if you'd otherwise prompt." The correct posture is uniform `RecipeMissingAnswerError`; the runtime's only synthesized answer is the interactive blank-multiselect path, which is a deliberate user action (§8.8.5 "empty selection allowed unless `validate.min: 1`").
  - `validate.min`/`validate.max` are reused across number prompts (numeric range) and multiselect prompts (selection-count range). Schema-level the shape is the same `Number` pair; runtime distinguishes by `prompt.type`. New per-type validators that want to reuse the existing schema slots (rather than introducing a new field) can follow this pattern without expanding `RecipePromptValidate`.
  - Schema fields that allow heterogeneous value types in choices (`RecipePromptChoice = String | Number | Boolean | { value, label, description? }`) need the runtime to try *literal-value match before any structural shortcut* (1-based index, char-prefix, etc.). A digit-only-→-index shortcut that runs before value match silently makes the entire numeric-choice subset of the schema unreachable. Always: literal value/label match first, structural shortcuts only as a fallback.

## [2026-05-18 22:23 CDT] - US-026 Review
- What was reviewed: ran `Skill(review-work)` 5-agent panel on commit f3ad3f6 (US-026 "Support built-in prompt types"). Cross-checked findings against spec §8.8.1 / §8.8.5 / §8.8.9 and the `RecipePrompt` schema in `sdk/src/schema/index.ts`.
- Files changed by this review fix: `core/src/cli/run.ts`, `core/src/recipes/prompts/runtime.ts`, `core/test/recipes/prompts/runtime.test.ts`.
- `review-work` findings:
  - fixed [BLOCKING goal-verifier / MAJOR code-quality / P1 QA]: `$bunfs` `init` handler in the compiled binary only parsed `--name=<value>` and `--answer=<key=value>` and silently dropped the space-separated forms (`--name <value>`, `--answer <key=value>`) that the OCLIF surface accepts and that the runtime's own remediation message recommends (`Provide it via --answer <name>=<value>`). Replaced the ad-hoc `find/filter` with the existing `parseStringFlag` loop pattern so both `--flag=value` and `--flag value` work, and `--answer` is repeatable in both forms. Verified manually: `core/dist/lando init --full --no-interactive --answer name=compiled-spaced` now scaffolds; `--answer=key=value` and `--name <value>` also still work.
  - fixed [BLOCKING context-mining / spec §8.8.1+§8.8.9]: `--yes` / `--no-interactive` were synthesizing answers for defaultless `confirm` (→`true`) and `multiselect` (→`[]`). Spec §8.8.1 explicitly says `--yes` "behaves like `--no-interactive` for unanswered prompts" and §8.8.9 step 4c says non-interactive resolution uses *the recipe's default*. Removed the `acceptScalarDefault` synthesis path so defaultless prompts under either flag now raise `RecipeMissingAnswerError`. `--yes` on a `confirm` with an explicit `default: false` still resolves to `false` (the recipe default), which matches the spec's "accepts every prompt's default" language.
  - fixed [BLOCKING context-mining / MAJOR code-quality / spec §8.8.5]: `multiselect` ignored `validate.min` and `validate.max`. Spec §8.8.5 says "Empty selection allowed unless `validate.min: 1`". Added `enforceMultiSelectBounds` that runs against both the supplied/answer path and the interactive blank-input path; non-interactive violations surface as `RecipePromptValidationError` (typed), interactive violations re-prompt with `Invalid value: select at least N item(s). Please try again.` so the recoverability requirement from AC #3 still holds.
  - fixed [MAJOR code-quality]: `select` resolution treated *any* all-digit input as a 1-based index lookup before attempting a literal value match, which made `RecipePromptChoice` number values unreachable (e.g. `choices: [80, 443, 8080]` with input `443` returned "index out of range" instead of value `443`). Swapped the order: try literal value/label match first; fall back to index only when no literal match exists. Added regression tests for both the literal-numeric-match and the index-fallback path.
  - fixed [P0 QA / MINOR code-quality]: runtime tests asserted `toBeInstanceOf(...)` only, not `_tag`. Added `_tag` assertions for every `RecipeMissingAnswerError` and `RecipePromptValidationError` rejection in `core/test/recipes/prompts/runtime.test.ts` so the tagged-error shape that `cli/run.ts`'s `commandErrorMessage` switches on is locked in.
  - rejected [BLOCKING goal-verifier] "CLI fixture tests do not cover each prompt type via `Bun.spawn`": the wired Alpha recipe (`node-postgres`) declares one prompt (`name`, type `text`). AGENTS.md explicitly documents the buffered-IO seam (`createBufferedPromptIO({ inputs })`) as the per-type CLI fixture pattern: *"Per-type prompt tests should use the buffered IO to script answers and assert `io.stdout()`/`io.stderr()` — no `Bun.spawn` round-trip needed."* `runtime.test.ts` drives `collectPrompts` (the actual CLI prompt collector) end-to-end for every Alpha type (`text`, `select`, `multiselect`, `confirm`, `number`, `secret`, `path`) with deterministic scripted input and captured transcripts; the CLI subprocess tests cover the wired type's full Bun.spawn round-trip. Building a synthetic recipe-injection harness purely to drive non-`name` prompts through Bun.spawn would require recipe-fixture infrastructure that is properly scoped to US-027 (cwd recipe source) / US-028 (canonical recipes). Per AC #1, "deterministic stdin/stdout" is satisfied by the buffered-IO surface.
  - rejected [BLOCKING context-mining / spec §8.8.5] "`when:` is accepted by schema but the runtime ignores it": honoring `when:` requires the §8.8.6 recipe expression engine (`{{ … }}` interpolation, control-flow blocks, the recipe render context with `answers.<name>`, `flags.<name>`, `host.*`, `env.*`, etc.) which is a much larger story. The current bundled recipe (`node-postgres`) has no `when:` on any prompt, and the schema was published in US-025 with `when: optional(String)` as part of the §8.8.3 surface so editor tooling can validate it. Out of US-026 scope; tracked for the expression-engine story.
  - rejected [MAJOR code-quality] "TTY raw-mode secret prompt uses a second async iterator over `stdin`": real concern but no wired Alpha recipe has a `secret` prompt yet (node-postgres declares only `name: text`). The shared-iterator hazard can only manifest when a `secret` prompt is followed by another prompt in a real TTY session; the buffered-IO test path that covers every type does not exercise the raw-mode reader. The correct fix is a `createStdioPromptIO` refactor where one reader owns all `stdin` consumption and raw-mode is a temporary toggle on the shared iterator — better scoped to the story that ships secret-bearing canonical recipes (US-028) so it can land with PTY regression coverage.
  - rejected [IMPORTANT context-mining / spec §8.8.5] "`path` prompt resolves against process cwd, not the destination directory": spec is correct, runtime is not — but the destination is `join(cwd, appName)` which depends on the `name` answer, and US-026 ships no `path` prompt in any wired recipe. Threading the resolved destination into `collectPrompts` (and handling the chicken-and-egg case where a `path` prompt precedes the `name` prompt in a recipe) is best done alongside US-028 when canonical recipes with path prompts land.
  - rejected [LOW security] "`--answer secret=value` exposes secrets via shell history / process argv": no Alpha recipe declares a `secret` prompt; the LOW recommendation is to avoid pointing users at `--answer` remediation text for secret prompts, which is a future-hardening item to apply when canonical recipes with secret prompts ship (US-028).
  - rejected [LOW security] "Answer/resolved maps should be `Object.create(null)` and prompt names should be schema-enforced kebab-case before US-027": `RecipePrompt.name` is currently `Schema.String`. The bundled string-literal recipe is trusted; the prototype-pollution exposure surface widens with US-027's cwd recipes, which is the right place to land the kebab-case constraint and the null-prototype maps together (matching the US-025 `guardKey` precedent for the parser).
  - rejected [LOW security] "ReDoS hardening on recipe `validate.pattern`": bundled-only recipes in Alpha; recipe-pattern length/input bounds belong with US-027's cwd source where the trust boundary actually changes.
  - rejected [LOW/INFO security] "`path` prompt traversal has no current filesystem sink": informational. Any future renderer/action that consumes a `path` answer for filesystem mutation will need a containment check; recorded against US-028.
  - rejected [WARN/MINOR] "`--answer foo=` accepts empty for text/secret without pattern": minor inconsistency with the interactive empty-value guard; recipe authors can use `validate.pattern` to enforce non-empty. Not blocking US-026.
  - rejected [MINOR] "Number parsing accepts scientific notation (`1e5`)": spec §8.8.5 just says "Integer or float". `Number(raw)` covers both. No exploitation path.
  - rejected [NITPICK] "Rename `acceptScalarDefault`": helper was deleted as part of the §8.8.1 / §8.8.9 fix above, so the naming complaint is moot.
- Verification run and result: lsp diagnostics clean on the three changed files; `bun run typecheck` passed (clean tsc -b); `bun run lint` passed (`biome check .` 348 files, no errors); `bun test` passed (704 pass / 11 skip / 0 fail / 3145 expect() calls; +18 tests, +25 expect() vs. the build step's 686 / 3120). Manual compiled-binary QA from `mktemp -d`: `core/dist/lando init --full --no-interactive --answer name=compiled-spaced` (space form) and `--answer=name=compiled-eq` (equals form) and `--name compiled-name` (space form) all scaffold the expected `.lando.yml`, `package.json`, `server.js`. Working tree clean after `bun run clean` apart from the three review-fix files.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - The `$bunfs` compiled-binary fast path in `core/src/cli/run.ts` must mirror the OCLIF flag surface *including* both `--flag=value` and `--flag value` forms; otherwise the runtime's own remediation messages contradict the binary's behavior. The reusable pattern is the existing `parseStringFlag(rest, i, name)` loop already in this file — never use `argv.find(arg => arg.startsWith("--flag="))`. Add this to the AGENTS.md "Compiled binary" gotcha when a future story trips on it.
  - Per spec §8.8.1 / §8.8.9, `--yes` is NOT "force every prompt to a truthy/empty value" — it is "accept every prompt's *declared* default without asking, otherwise behave like `--no-interactive`". Any synthesis fallback for a defaultless prompt under `--yes` violates the spec. The runtime now resolves answers from exactly three sources, in order: (a) `--answer key=value`, (b) recipe `default:`, (c) interactive prompt (if interactive). No fourth "guess" source.
  - `multiselect.validate.min/max` is per-selection-count, not per-element, and is enforced from a single helper (`enforceMultiSelectBounds`) that both `resolveMultiSelection` (supplied/answer path) and `runInteractivePrompt` (blank-input path) consult. Re-prompting on bounds violations in interactive mode preserves AC #3's recoverability.
  - `select` resolution must try literal value/label match *before* numeric-index fallback so number-valued choices (`choices: [80, 443]`) remain reachable. Schema permits `Schema.Number` choice values, so this is a real product surface even though the current bundled recipe only uses string choices.
  - `_tag` assertions on tagged errors (`RecipeMissingAnswerError`, `RecipePromptValidationError`) lock in the discriminant that the CLI's `commandErrorMessage` switch in `core/src/cli/run.ts` reads. `instanceof` alone is necessary but not sufficient — the tag is the wire shape.
  - Deferral pattern observed: when a finding points at a real gap (e.g., `when:` evaluator, `path`→destination resolution, TTY shared-stdin for secrets) but the gap manifests only with downstream story surfaces (US-027 cwd recipes, US-028 canonical recipes with path/secret prompts, US-029 expression engine), it is correct to record the deferral with the specific landing story rather than ship a half-fix now. Two precedents already in this repo: the US-025 `__proto__` parser guard for the recipe source we already had, vs. the broader kebab-case/null-prototype hardening deferred to US-027 (cwd boundary); and the US-025 `deprecated:` field rejected pre-decode rather than implemented before §18 lands.

- Files changed: `core/build.config.ts` (added `node-postgres` to `bundledRecipes`), `core/src/recipes/source.ts` (new resolver), `core/src/recipes/bundled.ts` (generated), `scripts/build-bundled-recipes.ts` (new generator with trailing `biome format --write`), `scripts/codegen.ts` (registered `bundled-recipes`), `package.json` (added `codegen:bundled-recipes` script), `core/src/cli/commands/init.ts` (loads recipe through `resolveRecipeRef`, unwraps Effect with `runPromiseExit` + `Cause.failureOption`, recipe-agnostic error messages), `core/src/cli/oclif/commands/apps/init.ts` (wires `--recipe` flag and maps tagged errors to stderr), `core/src/cli/run.ts` (compiled `$bunfs` path parses `--recipe` and renders `NotImplementedError` + `RecipeManifestNotFoundError`), `core/test/recipes/source.test.ts`, `core/test/recipes/bundled.test.ts`, `AGENTS.md`, `spec/alpha/prd.json`, `spec/alpha/progress.txt`.

- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: codegen scripts that emit into `core/src/**` must shell out to `biome format --write` on the output file before exiting, otherwise the existing `core/test/build/biome.test.ts` and any branch that lands new bundled entries will hard-fail `bun run lint`.
  - Gotchas encountered: `Effect.runPromise` on a failure rejects with `FiberFailure` wrapping the tagged error; callers that need `instanceof NotImplementedError`/`instanceof RecipeManifestNotFoundError` must run via `Effect.runPromiseExit` + `Cause.failureOption` and rethrow the inner failure.
  - Useful context: `core/build.config.ts#bundledRecipes` is the single ship-list for built-in recipes; adding an entry there + `core/src/recipes/builtin/<id>/manifest.ts` exporting `<ID>_RECIPE_ID`, `<id>RecipeSource`, `<id>RecipeYaml` is enough for `bun run scripts/build-bundled-recipes.ts` to regenerate `core/src/recipes/bundled.ts` deterministically.

## [2026-05-18 23:38 CDT] - US-027 Review
- Reviewed the US-027 build commit (HEAD `9139649 feat: Ship cwd-only recipe source`) via `Skill(review-work)` with 5 parallel agents (Oracle goal-verifier, Oracle code-quality, Oracle security, unspecified-high context-mining, unspecified-high hands-on QA). Cross-checked findings against PRD-04 US-027 acceptance criteria, spec §8.8.3/§8.8.4, and the US-026 deferral log.
- Files changed by review: `core/src/recipes/source.ts` (id↔basename enforcement + tagged IO failures), `core/src/cli/oclif/commands/apps/init.ts` (map `RecipeManifestValidationError`), `core/src/cli/run.ts` (compiled `$bunfs` path maps `RecipeManifestValidationError`), `core/test/recipes/source.test.ts` (basename-mismatch test, quoted-id test, tarball/http URL rejection tests), `AGENTS.md` (gotcha extended), `spec/alpha/progress.txt` (this entry).
- `review-work` findings:
  - fixed [BLOCKING context-mining / spec §8.8.3 + US-026 deferral]: directory-resolved recipes did not enforce that `recipe.yml`'s top-level `id:` matches `basename(resolved.root)`. A local `./expected-id/recipe.yml` with `id: wrong-id` was being parsed successfully. The US-026 review log (line 3208) explicitly deferred this hard requirement to "US-027's cwd-only source", and US-027 was the landing story. Added a regex-based top-level `id` extractor in the resolver and a tagged `RecipeManifestValidationError` failure with the directory basename in `message` and an entry in `issues[]`. The check fires before the schema parser because the directory boundary is only known to the resolver. CLI smoke confirmed: `--recipe=./expected-id` with `id: wrong-id` exits 1 with the structured message + issue line.
  - fixed [MAJOR code-quality]: `resolveLocal` used `Effect.promise(() => file.exists())` / `Effect.promise(() => file.text())`. `Effect.promise` treats rejections as defects, so a readable existence check followed by an unreadable file (EACCES, EISDIR, EIO) produced a `Cause.failureOption(None)` defect that bypassed the tagged-error contract and surfaced via the `Cause.pretty` fallback in `init.ts#loadRecipeManifest`. Swapped both calls to `Effect.tryPromise` with a `readFailure(cause, manifestPath, verb)` helper that maps to `RecipeManifestNotFoundError` with a "Could not stat/read recipe.yml at …" message preserving the underlying cause text. `resolveLocal`'s error type is now `RecipeManifestNotFoundError | RecipeManifestValidationError` and `resolveRecipeRef`'s union widened to include it.
  - fixed [PARTIAL goal-verifier / AC1 literal wording]: PRD-04 AC1 names "git, tarball, npm, registry" as the rejected remote schemes. The spec §8.8.4 scheme set has no `tarball:` syntax, but the AC wording deserves explicit test coverage. Added three remote-rejection table rows: `tarball:https://example.test/recipe.tgz`, `https://example.test/recipe.tgz`, `http://example.test/recipe.tar.gz`. All three fall through `detectScheme` → "unknown" → `NotImplementedError` with the same Beta remediation, so the user-facing contract for tarball/archive refs is now pinned by test.
  - rejected [WARN goal-verifier] "Local recipe rendering still uses hardcoded node-postgres renderers; `initApp` discards `resolved.root`": out of scope. US-027's title is "Ship cwd-only recipe source"; the story explicitly delivers the source resolver, and acceptance criteria 1-3 are all about source resolution and bundling. Recipe file rendering (resolving a recipe's declared `files:` list against `resolved.root` for local recipes, expression interpolation in templates, `landofile.ts` programmatic output) is owned by US-028 (canonical recipes) and US-029 (`landofile.ts` programmatic output). The build step's existing manual QA in this story covers exactly the resolver surface plus the wired bundled renderer path.
  - rejected [WARN goal-verifier] "The no-network test name claims more than the test asserts (it only replaces `globalThis.fetch`, not spawned `curl/wget/git`)": the resolver imports zero process-spawning APIs (`node:child_process`, `Bun.spawn`, etc.) — a `grep -rn "spawn\|exec" core/src/recipes/source.ts` is empty. The fetch-replacement sentinel is the determinism guard; the absence-of-spawn-imports is a static structural property. Renaming the test would not improve coverage.
  - rejected [P0 QA] "All source and compiled remote-scheme rejections lack the literal `NotImplementedError` tag string in stderr": false-positive expectation. The tagged error's `_tag` discriminant exists for `instanceof` / switch dispatch in `core/src/cli/run.ts` (per AGENTS.md "Tagged errors" gotcha and the US-026 progress entry); it is not contractually rendered in stderr. The current CLI emits `${error.message}\n${error.remediation}` for every tagged error including `InitTargetExistsError`, `RecipeMissingAnswerError`, `RecipePromptValidationError`, and `NotImplementedError` — this is consistent across the entire init flow. Tests assert `instanceof NotImplementedError` against the SDK class, not stderr substring.
  - rejected [P0 QA] "Unknown bundled bare id `does-not-exist` returns `RecipeManifestNotFoundError` instead of `NotImplementedError`": the test contract is exactly the opposite. `core/test/recipes/source.test.ts` "unknown bare id fails with RecipeManifestNotFoundError listing known ids" asserts `instanceof RecipeManifestNotFoundError` and the known-ids list. A bare kebab id is a valid `builtin` scheme — what's missing is the *id within that scheme*, not the scheme itself.
  - rejected [P2 QA] "`--recipe=.` should be tagged"/"Repeated `--recipe` flags should be deterministic last-wins": `.` does not match any local prefix (`./`, `../`, `/`, `~/`) and is not a valid kebab id, so falls to "unknown" → `NotImplementedError` (correct behavior). OCLIF's "Flag --recipe can only be specified once" is framework-default duplicate-flag rejection — re-implementing last-wins for one flag would be inconsistent with the rest of the CLI surface.
  - rejected [QA] "Stderr formatting differs source vs compiled (OCLIF prefixes `Error:`, compiled does not)": pre-existing OCLIF wrapping behavior, applies to every CLI error path, not introduced by US-027.
  - rejected [IMPORTANT context-mining] "§8.8.4 says recipes accept the same source schemes as includes, which list `gitlab:`/`bitbucket:`; resolver currently treats those as `unknown` instead of `git`": user-facing behavior is identical (NotImplementedError + Beta remediation). The classification string ("scheme \"gitlab\"" vs "scheme \"unknown\"") only matters when the remote-source story actually lands (Beta), at which point each scheme will need its own resolver path anyway. Classification nit; defer to the Beta remote-source story.
  - rejected [IMPORTANT context-mining] "`../path` and `~/path` are accepted but undocumented": both are conservative `local` defensive extensions; behavior is correct, just under-documented. AGENTS.md gotcha covers `./path`/`/abs/path` as the canonical Alpha forms; `../` (parent-relative) and `~/` (home-relative) are convenience extensions that already pass the basename check. No spec violation, no behavior bug. Documentation polish belongs in the AGENTS.md edit for the next story that surfaces it.
  - rejected [IMPORTANT context-mining] "`apps:init` spec §8.8.1 requires bootstrap=`minimal` but `initSpec.bootstrap` is `commands`": pre-existing init-command metadata mismatch, not introduced by US-027. The custom `run()` override bypasses the bootstrap-driven `runEffect` path, so the practical effect is nil. Belongs to a future spec-alignment story for `apps:init` metadata.
  - rejected [FYI context-mining] "Bundled recipe codegen embeds only manifest strings, not the full recipe filesystem": correct for the current renderer path (bundled `node-postgres` files come from `core/src/recipes/builtin/node-postgres/index.ts` constants, not from `recipe.yml`'s `files:` list). The codegen surface will need to expand for US-028's canonical recipes that ship templates; that's a US-028 concern.
  - rejected [MINOR code-quality] "Exhaustive `never` guard after the scheme switch": the existing `switch(scheme)` covers every branch of the `RecipeRefScheme` union; TypeScript's `noImplicitReturns` already catches any missed branch. Belt-and-suspenders nit.
  - rejected [MINOR code-quality] "Codegen identifier validation in `scripts/build-bundled-recipes.ts`": current id format is constrained by the manifest-file lookup (`core/src/recipes/builtin/${id}/manifest.ts` must exist and export the specific symbols). A digit-prefixed id would fail at module-import time with an `Identifier expected` TS error. Premature.
  - rejected [NITPICK code-quality] "`ResolvedRecipe.root: string | undefined` should be a discriminated union": fine for current consumers; tighten when US-028/US-029 add consumers that branch on local-vs-bundled root.
  - rejected [LOW/FYI security] "Optional manifest size limit before `file.text()`": Alpha local recipes are user-controlled; the user already chose to point `--recipe` at the directory. The size guard makes sense once Beta lands remote sources where the source bytes come from a remote actor.
- Verification run and result: lsp_diagnostics clean on every changed `.ts` file; `bun run typecheck` passed (tsc -b clean); `bun run lint` passed (biome check 353 files, no fixes); `bun run codegen` produced no diff (drift gate clean — bundled-plugins, bundled-recipes, oclif-manifest, ci-workflow all idempotent); `bun test` passed (730 pass / 11 skip / 0 fail / 3300 expect(), +5 tests +33 expect() vs. the build step's 725/3267). Manual CLI smoke confirmed: source CLI with `--recipe=./expected-id` and `id: wrong-id` in `recipe.yml` exits 1 with `Recipe id "wrong-id" must match the directory basename "expected-id" ... - id: "wrong-id" must equal directory basename "expected-id"`; `--recipe=tarball:https://example.com/recipe.tgz` exits 1 with the `unknown` scheme + Beta remediation message.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - The "lightweight id extraction" pattern (`/^id:[ \t]+(?:"([^"]+)"|'([^']+)'|([^\s#]+))[ \t]*(?:#.*)?$/m`) at the source-resolver layer is the right place to enforce spec §8.8.3 — the manifest parser cannot do it because it has no knowledge of the resolved root directory. A future "kebab-case for prompt names" enforcement (the other US-025 deferral) will need the same dual-layer treatment: cheap structural check at the boundary that owns the trust transition, with the full schema parser as the canonical validator.
  - `Effect.promise` is a footgun for any IO that can legitimately fail. The pattern is `Effect.tryPromise({ try, catch: cause => new TaggedError({...preserve cause.message...}) })` everywhere a Bun/Node IO call appears inside an Effect generator. The cost of wrapping is ~3 lines per call and the win is "any error reaches the caller as a tagged failure", which `cli/run.ts` and `cli/oclif/commands/apps/init.ts` rely on for typed dispatch.
  - When AC wording (e.g., AC1 "git, tarball, npm, registry") references a scheme that the spec does not formally define (the spec §8.8.4 scheme set has no `tarball:` entry), the correct compromise is to (a) make sure the catch-all "unknown" branch produces the same tagged-error + Beta remediation a named branch would, and (b) add explicit test coverage for the named-but-unspecified scheme so the AC wording is verifiable. Don't invent a new scheme branch without spec backing.
  - Deferral landing protocol: when an earlier story's review log explicitly defers a hard spec requirement to a *named* later story (here US-025 → US-027 for id↔basename), the review of that landing story must check for the deferral. The `progress.txt` `rejected ...` entries are the search index — `grep -n "deferred\|defer" spec/alpha/progress.txt` before reviewing is cheap insurance.
